  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_71626cc1-1f30-4e40-bf1c-5a12015b5812'

  <span id="freeText1604858801995949798" style="display:none">My name is Tate. He doesn't call me that, though. He would never refer to me so informally, if he referred to me at all. No, he'll barely even speak to me.<br /><br />But he still won't leave me alone.<br /><br />We were best friends once. Then he turned on me and made it his mission to ruin my life. I've been humiliated, shut out, and gossiped about all through high school. His pranks and rumors got more sadistic as time wore on, and I made myself sick trying to stay out of his way. I even went to France for a year, just to avoid him.<br /><br />But I'm done hiding from him now, and there's no way in hell I'll allow him to ruin my senior year. He might not have changed, but I have. It's time to fight back. <br /><br />I'm not going to let him bully me anymore.<br /><br />***This novel contains adult/mature young adult situations. It is only suitable for ages 18+ due to language, violence, and sexual situations.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691157681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11722145368431905194"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412193i/810513.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>I am conducting what I'm shelving as a "New Adult (NA) Experiment". I'm going to work my way through some of the popular New Adult books and see if I can weed out the crap and hopefully find some surprising gems. Here's hoping!</i><br/><br/>Dear book,<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436476662ra/15465366.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I was ready to like this book. I was ready to be forgiving of the small negatives. I was ready to make excuses for it, try and justify the bad and pretend the good overshadowed it. I don't even remember the last time I wanted to like a book this much. Despite wha</span>
  <span id="freeText11722145368431905194" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412193i/810513.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I am conducting what I'm shelving as a "New Adult (NA) Experiment". I'm going to work my way through some of the popular New Adult books and see if I can weed out the crap and hopefully find some surprising gems. Here's hoping!</i><br><br>Dear book,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436476662ra/15465366.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was ready to like this book. I was ready to be forgiving of the small negatives. I was ready to make excuses for it, try and justify the bad and pretend the good overshadowed it. I don't even remember the last time I wanted to like a book this much. Despite what you may think from my reactions to most books in the NA experiment, I don't just spend my time looking for things to bitch and moan about in these books. I'm looking for the NA books which are different and actually tell a good story, even if it is a romance. This book's description didn't sound like the others that are all virtually identical. So, I wanted to love it. I really tried. But I couldn't. There were too many things. The negatives were flying at me on every page and, after a while, I couldn't ignore them. Which is sad. <br><br>We started on reasonably good terms. I really liked the idea of the book for two reasons: 1) I wanted to see how the author handled the subject of bullying and 2) I was intrigued by the promise of a bully being turned into someone we could love. The book didn't really deliver on either of those. For the former, the book started by using a chapter to give us an example of the way Tate had been bullied for several years by a guy who used to be her best friend but turned on her. It was sad, it was awful and I felt sorry for her. Objective achieved. Then we cut to a year later when she comes back from a year studying in France, determined not to let him win this time around. What this book then became was a showdown between two beautiful people who clearly wanted to shag but decided the best kind of foreplay is that where they antagonize the hell out of each other. It wasn't really a story about bullying, it was just about them each trying to get one up on the other. <br><br>As for the second reason I was attracted to this book, Jared (the guy) did win me over to some extent. I feel a bit strange about it because, on the one hand, I can see why he behaved like he did and I can find some level of forgiveness for him. But I'm not really able see a) why Tate forgave him so easily and b) why he changed back so abruptly (I don't think Tate's class monologue was a convincing enough reason). The reasons for his behaviour make sense, but his progression back to how he was before and the HEA don't. The main problem - and I shouldn't be surprised by this - is that the author doesn't attempt to humanize him first. That would have made it a better book and a more believable story. But instead of being humanized, Jared is sexualized first. And using his hot body as an excuse for forgiveness didn't work because that's not a good enough reason and I don't find this an attractive description of a man: <b>"I doubt you even wait until the condom's off before forgetting their names."</b> There must be something wrong with me.<br><br>But anyway. This stuff wouldn't have been enough for a one star rating on its own. With just this, I would have given at least two stars, maybe even three on a good day. The problem I had, the HUGE fucking problem I had with this book was the protagonist. God, she was the very meaning of insufferable. And her best friend wasn't far behind. On that subject, this seems to be incredibly common in NA books: BBF (Bad Best Friend) Syndrome. It's like a requirement for the protagonist's best friend to encourage them to forget about all the bad stuff a guy has done, just forget that he's a total jerk because he is SO HOT. Jared harassed Tate for years and yet her best friend advises her to get together with him and, when she doesn't, decides to have a go herself! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409700653ra/11010717.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Forget the best friend, let's get back to the high-and-mighty queen of preciousness herself. Tate views everyone but herself, her parents and Jared with utter disdain. Being inside her head was like waging a war against every other female because of the things they wore, the things they said, and the guys they were with. For one, I feel it is always best to avoid stupid phrases like <b>"queen bee of the mean girls"</b>, but it was when she referred to everyone Jared was with as being "slutty" because they were all over him that I felt like someone had really lit my fuse. She walks onto every scene, describing the others as "slutty looking girls". If they weren't sluts, they were bitches or "twits", every woman is an enemy to Tate in this book - even her "best friend" isn't immune. Piper, the girl Jared uses and casts aside, gets the worst of it: <b>"Piper had her face buried in his neck. She looked trashy in her short, tight black dress and heels. Who wore heels to the beach?"</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419015611ra/12967360.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Look, I go to a University that used to be an all female institution. It's not anymore, but there are still currently around two women to every one guy. I know women. Smart women, stupid women, extroverted women, shy women, ambitious women, funny women, geeky women, sporty women, straight women, gay women... and I don't believe that I have ever seen a single woman as vapid, shallow and senseless as all the ones who exist in this novel. They walk around with their breasts bulging out, drooling over men who only love the marvellous Tate (who is, naturally, above all this breast-bulging, drooling business). I guess it's bad that I find myself siding with the antagonist in all this. And don't even get me started on that ridiculous fight in the school corridor between Tate and Piper.<br><br>There is so much slut-shaming, woman-shaming and obsessing over virginity in this book. For Tate, her virginity is a gift-wrapped present to be given to the one most deserving, while having sex with multiple guys is shameful. This quote is a particular favourite of mine: <b>"I'd been called a bitch before, and it didn't hurt the way being called a slut did. Being a bitch could be a survival technique. They get respect. There was no honor in people thinking you were a slut."</b> Reading that was a bit like dying a painful, anti-feminist death.<br><br>But wait! Just when you thought the guys got to escape Tate's judgement because of their penises, she casts a withering glance over them and their stupid ways. Honestly, she is the most annoying character ever. <b>"The girls had no other interests beside shopping and makeup and the guys here gave me the urge to sanitize my eyeballs after seeing the way they looked at me."</b> For godsake, Ms Precious, go sanitize your eyeballs somewhere we don't have to hear you whining, here you go, use this acid.<br><br>Tate's thoughts when Ben came to talk to her and tried to be nice were particularly annoying too. He was really sweet and lovely, didn't judge her on the rumours, and just wanted a conversation. And what is Tate thinking about these niceties? She is inwardly cringing at him because he likes country music. What a moron. Whereas jackass who takes pleasure in humiliating her at least likes "cool" music. Moron. Tate, I hope you fall into a burning <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mIBTg7q9oNc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ring of fire</a>, down down down with the flames going higher, and I hope you <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nW3FsMQd23w" rel="nofollow noopener">stand by your man</a> until <s>Piper</s> <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vWy5_H3xrUQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Jolene</a> steals him. Then you'll be all <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=r8b8I2_Ik3E" rel="nofollow noopener">blue eyes crying in the rain</a>, dreaming of what you'll do with a <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8kAU3B9Pi_U" rel="nofollow noopener">subway token and a dollar tucked inside your shoe</a>. I can't think of a reason to use the words <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Tw5LaEzEcJw" rel="nofollow noopener">"you've got to know when to hold 'em, know when to fold 'em"</a> but I'm going to anyway. And, really, who needs a reason for anything beyond: because <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eEH2lux-iuE" rel="nofollow noopener">tractors are sexy</a>. <br><br>And, on that note, I shall depart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11722145368431905194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_660417124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660417124" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/660417124?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=book-1-of-my-fav-series">book-1-of-my-fav-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660417124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12246800797153355407"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428140i/856414._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428140i/856415.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong><i>Bully </i> was a wonderfully addictive read that kept my heart racing from start to finish. I could not put it down! 5 stars!!</strong><br/><br/><em>He loves me... He loves me not... He loves me... He loves me not...</em><br/><br/>Jared and Tate grew up next door to each other. Jared was sweet, generous and friendly and they were the best and closest of friends. But not anymore. The kid who had held her hand through the pain of losing her mother, who had climbed trees with her, and who had snuck over for sleepovers was gone and now he s</span>
  <span id="freeText12246800797153355407" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428140i/856414._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428140i/856415.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong><i>Bully </i> was a wonderfully addictive read that kept my heart racing from start to finish. I could not put it down! 5 stars!!</strong><br><br><em>He loves me... He loves me not... He loves me... He loves me not...</em><br><br>Jared and Tate grew up next door to each other. Jared was sweet, generous and friendly and they were the best and closest of friends. But not anymore. The kid who had held her hand through the pain of losing her mother, who had climbed trees with her, and who had snuck over for sleepovers was gone and now he seemed to live solely to torment her.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"Every party we go to, or every time I relax at school, there's some prank or embarrassment to ruin it."</em>
</blockquote><br>The title of this book did not lie! The hero genuinely was a bully in the first part of the book and to be honest, I wasn't sure how I was ever going to fall for him. He was <em>mean</em>. Not like violent or abusive or anything, but the things he said and did were genuinely hurtful and unkind.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <em>"Even after everything he'd done, part of me still missed that boy who was my waking thought and constant companion as a kid. But that Jared was gone now. In his place was a sour, hateful douchbag that had no regard for me."</em>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But the real question that I kept asking myself was... <strong>
  <em>why?</em>
</strong><em> </em>As a general rule, behavior like his is a result of some sort of extreme hurt but for the life of her, Tate couldn't figure out what she did to wrong him and she was hurting deeply both for their lost friendship and for the pain he was causing in her life.<br><br>Now, because the story was told entirely from Tate's perspective, it was a while before I got to discover what had made Jared turn into a bully which left me plenty of time to wonder at the possibilities...<br><br>Everything about him was just so contradictory. He blared music late at night so she couldn't sleep but covered for her at school when she was in trouble. He made sure none of the guys at school ever touched yet and yet clearly didn't want her for himself. I kept trying to figure him out. Maybe it was his messed up way of trying to protect her? Maybe he didn't feel good enough for her and was trying, in the only way he knew how, to look out for her?<br><br>A part of me couldn't help but try to rationalize or at least understand what was going on inside his head because the more I read, the more it was clear that his actions were not just straight up meanness. There was something more behind it. Misguided and wrong perhaps but I could sense something... 'good' in him maybe? Although at first I wondered if maybe that was just my natural desire to redeem the hero of my book... needless to say, it stirred up a lot of questions and kept me totally hooked and curious to see where the story would go next.<br><br>I also really want to point out how much I loved the heroine. She was smart, sassy and certainly no pushover. Given the 'bullying' theme of the book and how she was the victim of it, I was curious how she's react to it all and was pleasantly surprised to see how much she fought back and stood her ground. She even had several badass moments and certainly earned my respect as a character. In her own words: <em>"I wasn't a whiner and I didn't want to be rescued."</em> &lt;--- yup! I loved her!<br><br>This book will make you see where bullies come from and show you how a perfectly sweet and loving person can be shaped into a tormentor.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"This is how bullies are made."</em>
</blockquote><br>The author did a phenomenal job of portraying Jared. She managed to capture his conflict in subtle ways that were just strong enough to keep you guessing at his real motivations behind his actions. He was clearly being a bully but at the same time, it was also clear that he wasn't a bad guy.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"There was a time when I had all his attention and I loved it. And as much I wanted him to leave me alone, I also liked..the way he was looking at me right now. And then I remembered that I hated him."</em>
</blockquote><br>I will say though that despite everything going on between them - Jared and Tate had some seriously chemistry!! Talk about unresolved sexual tension! I mean really! But I loved that despite everything he did while he was being mean, that he never crossed the line into touching her... that again was more proof to me of him feeling something deeper for her.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>"Don't touch me." I'd meant to yell, but it came out as a whisper.<br></em>
  </strong>
  <br>
  <strong> <em> Jared moved his head from side to side trying to catch my eyes, his lips inches from my fave. "If I ever lay my hands on you," he said low and husky, "you'll want it."</em></strong>
</blockquote><br>I really hated myself for admitting it, but despite the bullying, he made my heart flutter. Wrong. Wrong. Wrong. I know. But still... *flutter*<br><br>I loved the way the author subtly included little elements and details that made me fall for him while he was being a bully but yet that also didn't excusing his actions. She made it clear to the readers that there was something deeper beneath the surface... something that the heroine couldn't quite see at first.<br><br>Parts of the book just had me grinning like crazy - almost in a way that was a little reminiscent of the Neighbor from Hell books but.. in high school. Gah! It felt wrong but I just couldn't stop smiling in certain places. But then something would happen that would sober me right up.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"I hate you!" I screamed at his face and meant every word...<br></em>
  <br>
  <em> "Good!" he shouted in my face, boring down on me. "Finally. Because it's been a long time since I could stand the sight of you... I promise you will be in tears by next week."</em>
</blockquote><br>Little by little, Tate began to piece together bits of his life... a life she hadn't been a part of since his 'change' at fourteen. She begins to notice things... scars on his back, subtle ways that he protected her... and yet none of it quite added up.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"When Jared was fourteen, his father called and asked if Jared could come and visit him for the summer. Happily, Jared agreed and left for eight weeks. After that visit, though, he returned cold and cruel."</em>
</blockquote><br>But I still just couldn't figure Jared out. Did he like her (somewhere <em>deep</em> down inside)? Did he hate her (unlikely, based on his actions and words)? What made him so angry with her? Why did he want to hurt her? Why did he want to protect her? ... Questions. Questions. Never-ending questions. I needed to know WHY!<br><br>This book also had a lot of deeper issues going on as well. When someone is bullied, how far do they get pushed before they retaliate? And, by doing so, are they not themselves just perpetuating the cycle by becoming a bully themselves? Or is it self-defense? Is it justified? Understandable? Necessary? Completely wrong? Where were the lines drawn?<br><br>I was nervous going into this book... could I fall for a bully? Did I even want to? I hate bullying. It makes me sick. But I could sense from early on that Jared was a little different. He certainly wasn't all bad and his actions weren't random... and something about him made me desperate to find out what had happened to him to make him the way he was. It had to have been bad...<br><br>When his backstory came out, it broke my heart. Completely. It explained everything. It of course didn't excuse it, but knowing what had happened in his life, you could at least understand where he was coming from.<br><br>But at the same time I absolutely adored how, despite the tragedy of it, Tate didn't just fall into a weepy heap and accept him back. He had seriously wronged her (regardless of his reasons) and she made him work to earn her forgiveness.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"I'm sorry," he whispered. "I know I can make this up to you. Don't hate me."</em>
</blockquote><br>The book took me through a range of emotion and even left me teary in places seeing the friendship they'd once had, the hurt that was left over, the anger that was thrown around and the hearts that were left bruised.<br><br>This was one of those books that made me want to slow down and pace myself so that I didn't finish it too soon. The story sucked me in, made me <em>care</em>, and totally absorbed me in these characters' lives and journeys. I loved every word.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <em>"Are you mine?" I asked as I wiped me tears.<br></em>
    <br>
    <em> He kissed the corners of my mouth softly... "Always have been," he whispered.</em>
    <b></b>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is a New Adult book. There is steam and sex. The scenes are not fade-to-black, but yet also are not overly graphic. They're more emotional than anything.<br><br>There is definitely a happy ending here. No cliffhanger! But, this is the first of a series so it does leave room to explore their story further after this book so there is no epilogue. But still, I was left completely happy, satisfied and overflowing with warm, fuzzy emotions.<br><br><b> From start to finish, <i> Bully </i> grabbed a hold of my heart. I could not put it down. I could not stop turning the pages. My heart raced, broke, and healed. It was a unique twist on the bad boy meets good girl tale. Beautiful, painful and addictive. 5 stars!! <br><br>I honestly can't believe that this a debut novel! The writing was effortless and just allowed you to flow seemlessly through the story. I was very impressed and will certainly be looking out for more from Penelope Douglas.<br><br>Highly recommended! </b><br><br><i>... and OMG that was a long review!! </i> O_O <br><br>Casting (also see above): <br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428140i/856416._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428140i/856417._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1371573537l/18090508.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>************************************<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12246800797153355407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312922334p2/5477946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/653819679?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=authentic-and-realistic">authentic-and-realistic</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=mild-to-medium-steam">mild-to-medium-steam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=hero-needed-to-grovel-more">hero-needed-to-grovel-more</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer653819679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10652139364002604345"><b>3 Stars – I have very mixed emotions about this book.</b><br/><br/>While I liked this book for the most and was captivated by the author's realistic portrayal of bullying, I must admit, this book left me with mixed feeling. <br/><br/>Bullying is a real-life problem and I felt the author did a great job showcasing its powerful ability to hurt the human soul while at the same time showing the resilience of the human spirit. <br/><br/>For me, though, this book had some undeniable stumbling blocks. This story was too Young Adult for</span>
  <span id="freeText10652139364002604345" style="display:none"><b>3 Stars – I have very mixed emotions about this book.</b><br /><br />While I liked this book for the most and was captivated by the author's realistic portrayal of bullying, I must admit, this book left me with mixed feeling. <br /><br />Bullying is a real-life problem and I felt the author did a great job showcasing its powerful ability to hurt the human soul while at the same time showing the resilience of the human spirit. <br /><br />For me, though, this book had some undeniable stumbling blocks. This story was too Young Adult for my personal tastes. And while I felt Tate's character was well fleshed out, richly developed and multilayered, the rest of the cast of characters, including Jared, for me at least, seem at times one-dimensional. There was a lack of character development and character depth to them. They seemed to be locked into the scripted roles they were assigned. Because of that, I found it difficult to sympathize with Jared's plight and the reasons for his atrocious behavior once it was finally revealed; or, for that matter, to understand why Tate was so <i>willing</i> to forgive and forget all he'd done to her when he finally changed his actions. Sadly, I was never given enough reasons to fully like Jared's character. <br /><br />All in all, I'm glad I read this book. If you enjoy the Young Adult/New Adult genre then you will more than likely LOVE this story. Considering the characters were in high school, I would classify this book Young Adult. Definitely a mature Young Adult, as it was fairly steamy. <br /><br />Review posted at: <a href="http://sweptawaybyromance.blogspot.com/?m=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Swept Away By Romance</a> </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer661039615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18362319031676872174">First off, I admit: I'm a sucker for love/hate stories. And after reading the premise for <u>Bully</u>, I was super psyched to see where it would take me.<br/><br/>Alas, I feel like I've stepped into a trap.<br/><br/>I've come across a thousand FANFICTIONS that were so. much. better. (Hell, comparing it to that feels like an insult to fanfictions themselves.) But this is simply yet <i>another</i> blasted romance novel suffering from the 'new-adult-unoriginal-cliche-itis' that's been circulating around and contaminating 80% of th</span>
  <span id="freeText18362319031676872174" style="display:none">First off, I admit: I'm a sucker for love/hate stories. And after reading the premise for <u>Bully</u>, I was super psyched to see where it would take me.<br><br>Alas, I feel like I've stepped into a trap.<br><br>I've come across a thousand FANFICTIONS that were so. much. better. (Hell, comparing it to that feels like an insult to fanfictions themselves.) But this is simply yet <i>another</i> blasted romance novel suffering from the 'new-adult-unoriginal-cliche-itis' that's been circulating around and contaminating 80% of the contemporary books I've read. God, I believe this is the gazillionth time I'm labeling a story as 'cliche' which is making my limited vocabulary feel somewhat cliched- but there's just no other way to put it when all these books turn out to be the same! A pity, really, because I felt this storyline held so much potential.<br><br>The central focus of <u>Bully</u> sticks with the relationship between our severely annoying protagonist, <b>Tate</b> (and in case you were wondering, she's a she, and to furthermore weird you out, her full name's actually TATUM. I know, I know. *shakes head in exasperation* A little advice to you authors out there: if you're intending to pick an uncommon name for your main character, make sure you don't mix un<i>common</i> with un<i>usual</i>. It serves to be highly distracting throughout the entire read, especially when you have these guys constantly popping in your head:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474683501i/20631588._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474683930i/20631612.jpg" width="350" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">) <br><br>–and her best friend-turned-life ruiner, <b>Jared.</b> Two years into high school have been a living nightmare thanks to this guy and his ludicrous pranks and rumors (and I do mean ludicrous, because honestly, is the school comprised of absolute dimwitted idiots to believe all those blatantly false things about bowel diseases and STDs? Jesus fucking christ.) and for two whole years, she's done nothing to bring a stop to it.<br><br>Then one day, shes decides to pack up and leave for France for a gap year, and returns with no visible transformation in her personality— which really confuses me because wasn't that supposed to be the whole point? But oh wait, guess I missed out the part where she gets sprinkled in pixie dust and spontaneously develops a bout of confidence and tough-girl bitchiness to face her bully (not to mention the fact that all the guys at school seem to be dealing with a sudden infatuation with her despite treating her no better than a leper before). <br><br>Cue a slew of kneez to the ballz, snarky <s>t o t a l l y o r i g i n a l</s> comebacks and heated confrontations. But besides all this BS, the real kicker was that she was so fucking enraptured by his dreamy good looks and just <i>hubba hubba who cares that dickhead who heedlessly torments me for no apparent reason surpasses the douchiest of douchebags because my oh my look at those sweet set of abs!</i><br><br>WHAT IN THE WORLDS IS WRONG WITH YOU? I get that you were close to this guy in your tween days, but after the shit he's put you through, I think it's about time you sort yourself out and get. the fuck. over him. It's like she gets possessed by hormones every time she's around him, only to have said hormones abandon her next to practically any other guy. Especially Ben Jamison, who's not only charming and good-natured, but considered one of the most attractive hunks at school- and wonderful Tate here seemingly can't find a single fuck to give about him all due to the one lone fact that he has a taste for country music. Ugggh, where's my whip?<br><br>I can't even begin to tell you how awful it was having to bear with her narration! She deems it a necessity to hatefully label each and every female present in the story either a 'bitch' or a 'slut' or whatnot, but then takes pride in being considered one of those. According to her, she hasn't got any friends to hang out with, so I think it's safe to assume that Tate Brandt is an A+ judgemental son of a gun. Oh, and the only 'true friend' she does have is as shallow as they can get: people, I bring to you K.C! <s>Seriously, is it that hard to just stick with Casey or do you find some sort of satisfaction at being ~different~ by not doing that?</s><br><br>K.C., being fully aware of Jared's assholish mistreatments towards Tate, doesn't hesitate in pursuing him after falling victim for his perfect looks <i>*cringe*</i> and insists on her best friend to let go of the past and accept him for who he is (in case you didn't know: a manipulative bag of dicks). <i>*double cringe*</i> Obviously, it's only fitting that Tate should get supremely mad at her for the way she's acting- except it's for all the wrong reasons. Whether she's ready to believe it or not, she's jealous of K.C. and wants her paws off her man so to say (and do remember, said man is the same guy who's turned her into a social monstrosity).<br><br>The whole ordeal is just so bloody infuriating, all I wanted was some bleach to douse my- no wait, <i>their</i> eyes out with. Not a single character in the book that I could give less of a damn about! They were all just...so...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/641448.gif" width="500" height="289" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like I said before, the main focus was on the romance, which let me tell you, was just plain shitty. I felt no chemistry between Tate and Jared whatsoever and couldn't even find myself sympathizing much with his past (oh yes, did I not mention? Mr. Mysterious here has his very own secret <i>past</i> to strip away all his faults, how perfectly understandable!) <br><br>All my energy was just so directed towards my vexation at them, I couldn't take it anymore. The sole reason I even finished this off was to finally discover what had induced Jared's initial coldness towards Tate (spoiler alert: it's disappointing). And then I forced myself to reach the finish line with ragged breaths to see how the author planned on ending this because THERE'S ACTUALLY A SECOND BOOK???????? Gag me.<br><br>All in all, don't bother with this. <br>Just please. <br>Don't. <br>Rest assured, it's not going to be worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18362319031676872174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1365917650?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance">Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20871378-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365917650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer911850940383302959"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439931061r/15906305.jpg?v=1439931065056' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png' width='50' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>I had loved Jared once, but now I knew, without a doubt, that "my Jared" was gone.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439931393i/15906339.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>God. This book. I mean, <b>THIS BOOK</b>. Words fail me to describe just how much I loved this. I've had this in my kindle for what feels like ages since I got it as a freebie way back in 2013. I've seen it making the rounds on Goodreads and for some reason I still hadn't read it. If I can kick my own ass for not reading this sooner, I would, because this book? This book reminded me about all the reason</span>
  <span id="freeText911850940383302959" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439931061r/15906305.jpg?v=1439931065056" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">I had loved Jared once, but now I knew, without a doubt, that "my Jared" was gone.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439931393i/15906339.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>God. This book. I mean, <b>THIS BOOK</b>. Words fail me to describe just how much I loved this. I've had this in my kindle for what feels like ages since I got it as a freebie way back in 2013. I've seen it making the rounds on Goodreads and for some reason I still hadn't read it. If I can kick my own ass for not reading this sooner, I would, because this book? This book reminded me about all the reasons why I fell in love with New Adult romance to begin with. And I'm not talking about the manufactured angst, stupid decisions, at at times gratuitous sex scenes. No. I'm talking that all-encompassing feeling, just the right amount of gut-wrenching angst, you hate but love the hero, and you want to high five the heroine kind of read. It was like it was custom written just for me.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">This is how bullies are made...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439931393r/15906340._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Jared will be a hero that every reader will love to hate. I sure as hell did. But as much as I wanted to hate him, I can't deny that I was always wondering what was buried right below the surface to make him act the way he did because you just <i>knew</i> there had to be something. I have to say that Penelope Douglas did a phenomenal job with character development and that's what made the book as good as it was. The characters were multi-faceted and strongly developed. You get to know both of them as the story progresses and you also begin to understand both of them that much more.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439931859i/15906389._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>What truly made this book for me was Tate. She wasn't your typical NA heroine. This is a girl that had a backbone but didn't take it overboard. She wasn't intentionally cruel or flippant, she stood up for herself and she owned it. She was comfortable in her own skin and it was the perfect balance to the Jared's mercurial moods.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all of those things, and I loved you. But now? You're a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439932290ra/15906455.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I can't remember the last time a book kept me up all night, completely incapable of setting it down for even a second because I <i>needed</i> to know what happened next. I was sucked in from just the first chapter and read this in one sitting. This is exactly the kind of angst that I'm starving for. Imperfectly perfect, rage inducing and yet flawless. That probably doesn't even make sense, but if you're an angst whore like me, you'll know what I mean. My absolute favorite trope is the enemies-to-lovers, hate/lust thing and Bully delivers that in spades. While there were parts I wanted more from, I still can't rate it down for that simply because this book absolutely enthralled me. So much so, that I couldn't even bat an eyelash at any minor quibbles it may have had.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">We can be confused about what is good for us but not about what we truly want.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439932291i/15906456._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Simply put, it was amazing. Just amazing. This is a book that I recommend to any lovers of New Adult romance. I have found myself a new author to obsess over and my only regret is not reading this fantastic book sooner.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Yesterday lasts forever. <br>Tomorrow comes never.<br>Until you.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439932424ra/15906469.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>For more reviews visit<br><a href="http://dirtygirlromance.com" target="blogspot" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436477285i/15465455._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="911850940383302959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</b> The worst part about it? The summer before their freshman year of highschool, Jared went to stay with his dad. When he came home, he was different. He wan</span>
  <span id="freeText2350560321905853895" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Crazy good stars!!!!!</b><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/675d5263-c07e-436f-b425-ff16c4af2841_zpsa257d1c3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>For her whole high school career, Tate has been <b>bullied</b>. By one person in particular... <b>Jared</b>. Jared is Tate’s neighbor and used to be Tate’s best friend, but now, he isn’t. He is just someone who enjoys making her life hell. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/340a1bbb-32fd-4f26-bc86-93220a3f4f3b_zpsbac637a2.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851112.jpg" alt=" photo 340a1bbb-32fd-4f26-bc86-93220a3f4f3b_zpsbac637a2.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <blockquote>I had loved Jared once, but now I knew, without a doubt, that ‘my Jared’ was gone.</blockquote>
</b> The worst part about it? The summer before their freshman year of highschool, Jared went to stay with his dad. When he came home, he was different. He wanted nothing to do with Tate. And she has no idea why.<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/6b8f25cd-0002-4415-b678-9a15b9353bfb_zpsa346fa5c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851113.jpg" alt=" photo 6b8f25cd-0002-4415-b678-9a15b9353bfb_zpsa346fa5c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Thats the worst feeling in the world. To be that close to someone, to love them, and for them to start treating you terribly. It’s like she doesn’t even know him anymore. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/98a1faeb-cb73-4bd7-971c-511ce2fafd61_zpscba1adde.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851114.jpg" alt=" photo 98a1faeb-cb73-4bd7-971c-511ce2fafd61_zpscba1adde.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tate goes to Europe for her whole junior year. She sort of becomes her own while she is over there. She comes home for her senior year, ready to start fresh. She is determined to ignore Jared’s antics, have a good year, and make the most of her last year of high school. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/Bully-1bringmedown_zps0fe57ee5.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851115.jpg" alt=" photo Bully-1bringmedown_zps0fe57ee5.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She is sick of all of Jared and his friend’s crap. She won’t put up with it anymore. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/1b2434f2-2352-40b7-ac49-7a91c8dbafe3_zps8ce8b4c6.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851116.jpg" alt=" photo 1b2434f2-2352-40b7-ac49-7a91c8dbafe3_zps8ce8b4c6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tate is feisty. Strong willed. Tough. She was an awesome heroine. And Jared... Oh my Jared....<br>This may make me seem a little crazy- but I will just say it right now. <b>I LOVE JARED</b>. Okay, a lot of people loved Jared by the end of the book. Not me. I loved him <b>the entire time</b> I read this book. He was a jerk. An asshole. A bully. But there was just something about him that pulled me to him... I was rooting for him the whole book, so yay! <br>Once he said <i>“If I ever lay my hands on you, you’ll want it.”</i> I was a goner. Let me throw this out there. I don’t like ‘bullies’. Picking on people for any reason is not cool. There was just something about this guy... you could tell he and Tate had a love/hate thing going on, and I could tell there was some reason he was acting the way he was. <br><br>After Tate starts sticking up for herself, things start to change for her and Jared. Not at first, at first he is still just as determined to piss her off as ever. He even messes around with her best friend just to get a rise out of her. As the story builds, you can’t help but notice the sexual tension between these two, and the protectiveness Jared has over Tate. Eventually, things between them escalate. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/4653bcf6-5fd9-4e21-b819-ab3d86d7bf7e_zps2493c625.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851117.jpg" alt=" photo 4653bcf6-5fd9-4e21-b819-ab3d86d7bf7e_zps2493c625.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is hard for Tate to come to terms with. On one hand, this guy was her best friend for years. She has always loved him, she is very attracted to him. She just doesn’t think she can trust him. Jared still isn’t ready to open up to Tate. He doesn’t feel like he can tell her why he has been the way he has been all those years. All he can do is apologize. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I won’t hurt you. I’ll never hurt you again. I’m sorry.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>But is that ever going to be enough for Tate? Can she ever trust Jared, or is it all just some ploy to get to her again? <br><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/2baa6747-83f3-4df2-a0bb-250d76306c18_zpsa6e28adc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851118.jpg" alt=" photo 2baa6747-83f3-4df2-a0bb-250d76306c18_zpsa6e28adc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Once I started this book, I had trouble putting it down! It captivated me from the beginning. This is a topic not everyone is comfortable reading about, but I think it was pretty awesome that she went with it. And for being a YA book- there was some really nice steam in there ;)) <br>An emotional story about love, friendship, standing up for yourself, and forgiveness. A wonderful debut novel! <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/5929874a-3b73-4ac0-89e2-120dae949c59_zpsce6f5544.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426123i/851119.jpg" alt=" photo 5929874a-3b73-4ac0-89e2-120dae949c59_zpsce6f5544.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2350560321905853895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_646727496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646727496" />
    <a title="SueBee★bring me an alpha!★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha"><img alt="SueBee★bring me an alpha!★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528597635p2/15735368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646727496?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SueBee★bring me an alpha!★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SueBee★bring me an alpha!★" href="/user/show/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha">SueBee★bring me an alpha!★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to SueBee★bring me an alpha!★ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads">Geri Reads</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=series-g-contemporaries">series-g-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=series-cr-stand-alone">series-cr-stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=series-check-on-sequel">series-check-on-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=heroes-troubled-tortured">heroes-troubled-tortured</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=read-stand-alones-cr">read-stand-alones-cr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=read-contemporaries">read-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=kindle-freebie">kindle-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha?shelf=g-contemporaries">g-contemporaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646727496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8273605923134353380"><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/DouglasBullyTitlebySueBee_zps7ec4472a.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426154i/851228.jpg' alt=' photo DouglasBullyTitlebySueBee_zps7ec4472a.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20Sexy%20embrace/tumblr_mj90nm1buO1rdw96to1_500_zpsac62760f.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426154ra/851231.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mj90nm1buO1rdw96to1_500_zpsac62760f.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>★★★★! Bully, a debut by Penelope Douglas. Broken, jaded & sexy high school senior deals with the aftermath of having bullied a girl he can’t forget!</b><br/><br/><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br/><i>As the title would indicate this story is about bullying. And </i></span>
  <span id="freeText8273605923134353380" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/DouglasBullyTitlebySueBee_zps7ec4472a.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426154i/851228.jpg" alt=" photo DouglasBullyTitlebySueBee_zps7ec4472a.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20Sexy%20embrace/tumblr_mj90nm1buO1rdw96to1_500_zpsac62760f.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426154ra/851231.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mj90nm1buO1rdw96to1_500_zpsac62760f.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>★★★★! Bully, a debut by Penelope Douglas. Broken, jaded &amp; sexy high school senior deals with the aftermath of having bullied a girl he can’t forget!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><i>As the title would indicate this story is about bullying. And as irked and disgusted I am about anyone, I repeat anyone, picking on someone who is weaker, I feel that there are different types of bullying. When a boy likes a girl and picks on her is not the same as when a person is being targeted for being different, weak or not liked. Bully is a boy-likes-girl story, but it does in no way condone bullying, on the contrary.</i><br><br><b>Bully opens up with a Prologue at a party Tatum Brandt, Tate has decided to attend before her departure to study one year abroad.</b> It is revealed that Tate has been bullied all through high school by <b>her neighbor and former friend Jared Trent</b>. Jared and his friends play on last prank on Tate only underscoring her relief to be leaving.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>Thanks to Jared, my high school experience had been one long succession of rumors, pranks, tears, and disappointments.</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><b>Fast forward a year to Tate’s return for her senior year of high school</b>, she has changed. Though she clearly always must have been strong to endure the bullying, she is now projecting a new maturity, worldliness and confidence about her. That combined with Jared having come to the decision to no longer bully makes for a different experience at school. <b>The story follows them in the fall of their senior year through high school drama and events unfolding prompting them to delve into, relive and sort through the bullying that Tate had experienced</b>; The details of Jared’s and Tate’s friendship, fall-out, the aftermath and bullying will be revealed throughout the story. In addition there is <b>betrayal, self reflection and above all sexual tension and a budding romance</b>.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/DouglasBullyHerobySueBee_zps46a8facd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426154i/851229.jpg" alt=" photo DouglasBullyHerobySueBee_zps46a8facd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Jared Trent</b> has many qualities that make for a great hero; uncanny beauty, popular - clearly a charismatic leader - mysterious, sexy, damaged and elements of sinister. This is his story of redemption! For the first half of the book he had me at the edge of my seat. While the second half sort of fizzled. <br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“There were so many times when we were kids, growing up next door to each other, that I thought Jared was the greatest. He was sweet, generous, and friendly. And the most beautiful boy I’d ever seen.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>Six words to describe <b>Jared: Damaged, jaded, enigmatic, cynical, protective and immature</b>.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/DouglasBullyHeroinebySueBee_zpsaeb711b9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426154i/851230.jpg" alt=" photo DouglasBullyHeroinebySueBee_zpsaeb711b9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Tate Brandt</b> was a wonderful heroine, so strong and resilient, smart and mature. I loved everything about her. However I did not care for her “friend” K.C.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“There was a time when I had all of his attention and loved it. As much as I wanted him to leave me alone, I also liked how he seemed surprised. I liked the way he was looking at me right now. And then I remembered that I hated him.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>Six words to describe <b>Tate: Smart, strong, resilient, mature, good-hearted and forgiving</b>.<br><br><b>I really enjoyed Ms. Douglas writing style</b>. She has created a wonderful heroine and captivating hero. I was very much rooting for Jared and Tate. The sexual tension and build-up was spellbinding. The first half of the book had me glued, but the second half felt rushed and glossed over. <b>Bully left Jared and Tate in a good place.</b> The sequel will be about Jared’s friend Madoc who had a prominent part in this story. <b>Overall an excellent read!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Yesterday lasts forever. Tomorrow comes never. Until you.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>***<br>Hero rating: 4.5 stars <br>Heroine rating: 5 stars<br>Sex scenes rating: 4.5 stars<br>Sex scenes frequency: 3.5 stars<br>Storyline concept rating: 3.5 stars<br>Storytelling skills rating: 5 stars<br>Story ending rating: 3.5 stars<br>Book editing rating (5 = no edits spotted): 4 stars<br>************************************************<br><b>Overall rating: 4 stars<br><br>Would I recommend this book: Yes.<br>Would I re-read this book: Maybe later.<br>Would I read future books by this author: Yes.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20hands/tumblr_mp2hrx1SZI1sp7vtvo4_500_zps7765946d.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386628930ra/7409326.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mp2hrx1SZI1sp7vtvo4_500_zps7765946d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8273605923134353380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer834319530" class="readable"
              >

</a><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/><i>“I like storms. Thunder, torrential rain, puddles, wet shoes. When the clouds roll in, I get filled with this giddy expectation. Everything is more beautiful in the rain. Don’t ask me why. But it’s like this whole other realm of opportunity. I used to feel like a superhero, riding my bike over the dangerously slick roads, or maybe an Olympic athlete enduring rough trials to make it to the finish line.”</i><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/><a href='http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/51b11d65bb8bb46eeedf86cfb384eac8.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText4973317007400085465" style="display:none"><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/download-43.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><i>“I like storms. Thunder, torrential rain, puddles, wet shoes. When the clouds roll in, I get filled with this giddy expectation. Everything is more beautiful in the rain. Don’t ask me why. But it’s like this whole other realm of opportunity. I used to feel like a superhero, riding my bike over the dangerously slick roads, or maybe an Olympic athlete enduring rough trials to make it to the finish line.”</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/51b11d65bb8bb46eeedf86cfb384eac8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390860001i/8291891._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 51b11d65bb8bb46eeedf86cfb384eac8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>♦ <b>This book shivered my pulse. </b>♦<br>____________________________________________<br><br><i>“On sunny days, as a girl, I could still wake up to that thrilled feeling. You made me giddy with expectation, just like a symphonic rainstorm. You were a tempest in the sun, the thunder in a boring, cloudless sky. I remember I’d shovel in my breakfast as fast as I could, so I could go knock on your door. We’d play all day, only coming home for food and sleep. We played hide and seek, you’d push me on the swing, or we’d climb trees. Being your sidekick gave me a sense of home again.”</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/99788677c471152886ef44b91ffa5c39.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>♦ <b>This book tossed a hurricane into my lungs. </b>♦<br>____________________________________________<br><br><i>“You see, when I was ten, my mom died. She had cancer, and I lost her before I really knew her. My world felt so insecure, and I was scared. You were the person that turned things right again. With you, I became courageous and free. It was like the part of me that died with my mom came back when I met you, and I didn’t hurt anymore. Nothing hurt if I knew I had you.”</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/406c6d2199a44d0e1c57dab48368387f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390860001i/8291893._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 406c6d2199a44d0e1c57dab48368387f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>♦ <b>This book left crinkles at the corner of eyes like smiling wounds. </b>♦<br>____________________________________________<br><br><i>“Then one day, out of the blue, I lost you, too. The hurt returned, and I felt sick when I saw you hating me. My rainstorm was gone, and you became cruel. There was no explanation. You were just gone. And my heart was ripped open. I missed you. I missed my mom. What was worse than losing you was when you started to hurt me. Your words and actions made me hate coming to school. They made me uncomfortable in my own home.”</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/4706ecee2bca0cc3d54806dd926d5e40.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>♦ <b>This books left teeth marks in my bottom lip. </b>♦<br>____________________________________________<br><br><i>“Everything still hurts, but I know none of it is my fault. There are a lot of words that I could use to describe you, but the only one that includes sad, angry, miserable, and pitiful is ‘coward.’ In a year, I’ll be gone, and you’ll be nothing but some washout whose height of existence was in high school.”</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/a26a11fe4f633b2c97f65f97761dcc0c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390860001i/8291895._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo a26a11fe4f633b2c97f65f97761dcc0c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>♦<b> This book wrecked my eyelashes. </b>♦<br>____________________________________________<br><br><i>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all of those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but turns out that pricks in mustangs can still leave scars.”</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/e6d475b28a8a16e2388ed2fc099e68bb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>♦ <b>Probably one of the best books I’ve read in a very, <i>very</i> long time.</b>♦<br>____________________________________________<br><br>♦ <b>So. Yes, Penelope Douglas.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>You’re officially on my radar. </u>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2077465182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2077465182" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2077465182?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7345713-paloma-the-romance-queen">Paloma *The Romance Queen* </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=erotic-scenes">erotic-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077465182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16248245525491788180"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Hi, my name’s Melanie and all I want to read this summer is New Adult Romances. This is my third Penelope Douglas book and, again, I’m so impressed. I loved <i>Bully</i> and it might be my favorite book of hers I’ve read so far. <br/><br/>Before I go any further, I just want to point out again for people who follow my reviews mostly for the Fantasy I read: <b>I rate smutty books differently than o</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16248245525491788180" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Hi, my name’s Melanie and all I want to read this summer is New Adult Romances. This is my third Penelope Douglas book and, again, I’m so impressed. I loved <i>Bully</i> and it might be my favorite book of hers I’ve read so far. <br /><br />Before I go any further, I just want to point out again for people who follow my reviews mostly for the Fantasy I read: <b>I rate smutty books differently than other books!</b> I know many of the relationships are toxic and problematic and I completely understand that they wouldn’t be the healthiest and/or most ideal of starts for people in real life, but I love steamy reads and I rate them purely off my enjoyment. <br /><br />This all being said, <b>trigger warnings</b> for underage drinking and drug use, violence, descriptions of severe child abuse, and attempted rape. Also, I mean, this book is called <i>Bully</i>, and it is a book about a girl falling in love with her bully. There isn’t any major hazing or anything like that, but they both do some pretty mean things to one another. This is also a hate to love romance, but it’s kind of more like a love to hate to love romance, if that makes any sense, but no one writes hate to love as good as Penelope Douglas. <br /><br />Our main protagonist, Tatum (one of my favorite female names of all time), leaves for France for a year to study abroad. She hasn’t had the easiest life since her mom passed away from cancer. She once had a best friend who helped heal the wounds from the loss of her mother, but one day that greatest ally became her greatest enemy. <br /><br />Jared, Tatum’s now sworn enemy, lives next door to Tatum, and can’t stand the sight of any boy giving her any attention. When he’s not street racing, he’s making her life a living hell. This story surrounds them finishing their last year of high school, while they both try desperately to hide the feelings they have for one another and replace those feelings with hate. <br /><br />The only reason I’m not giving this five stars is because I really disliked Tatum’s best friend’s actions. K.C. not only does something she knows will upset her best friend, but she lies about. Then, once she gets caught, she continues to do it. Like, what a terrible representation of friendship (or maybe an accurate representation of high school friendships, let’s be real). And then, to make matters worse, it is all just swept under the rug, forgotten, and everyone is over it. Like, no, you don’t do that to your friend. No matter how bad you’re hurting, you don’t make it better by hurting others. <br /><br />The other thing is that there is a lot of slut shaming in this book. This is one of Penelope Douglas’ earlier books, and I haven’t noticed this in other things I’ve read by her, but there is a lot of judgement going on in this book when it comes to female promiscuity. Like, it doesn’t matter that these boys are all doing it, but they call out girls for sleeping with different guys a lot and it feels bad. Also, Tatum kind of borders on that “I’m not like other girls” line that is kind of gross, too. <br /><br />But both of these things are minor enough that it didn’t ruin this book for me. I actually really, really enjoyed it and I find myself wanting to read everything by Penelope Douglas. Her writing is seriously addicting and every one of her stories have been able to completely immerse me and evoke so much emotion from me. <br /><br />Also, it is important to note that obviously there is a lot of sexual content in this book, but all of the characters participating are 18+. Also, that first sex scene was 10/10. Like, sign me up for that now please. <br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16248245525491788180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
