<span id="freeTextContainer268569632904539440"><b>3,5 STARS</b><br/><br/><b>Yesterday lasts forever.<br/>Tomorrow comes never.<br/>Until you.</b><br/><br/>Tate and Jared are neighbours and they were best friends...<br/> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426399i/852018.jpg' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>One summer..Jared turned on Tate!He began to bully her..Spreading vicious rumours,humiliating her..Time passed and things get worst..<br/><br/><b>“What was worse than losing you was when you started to hurt me. Your words and actions made me hate coming to school. They made me uncomfortable in my own home.”</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426399ra/852019.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Tate comes back for her senior from France..But coming home she's tired of being </span>
  <span id="freeText268569632904539440" style="display:none"><b>3,5 STARS</b><br><br><b>Yesterday lasts forever.<br>Tomorrow comes never.<br>Until you.</b><br><br>Tate and Jared are neighbours and they were best friends...<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426399i/852018.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>One summer..Jared turned on Tate!He began to bully her..Spreading vicious rumours,humiliating her..Time passed and things get worst..<br><br><b>“What was worse than losing you was when you started to hurt me. Your words and actions made me hate coming to school. They made me uncomfortable in my own home.”</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426399ra/852019.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tate comes back for her senior from France..But coming home she's tired of being afraid and being a coward and letting him control her life.She takes her best friend K.C.'s advice and decides it's time to start fighting back!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426399i/852020.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>“Do you know what this is?” I took my middle finger and patted the corner of my eye with it. “It’s me, wiping away the last tear you’ll get.”</b><br><br><br>Jared is a complicated character.He is an arrogant playboy.At first Jared was jerk but when you learn more about him..you see that he is so sweet and charming.<br>I really liked seeing Tate's transition from being an introvert to someone who could completely hold her ground.I love the way she made sure no one messed with her.I thought she did an amazing job standing up for herself.<br><br>The sexual contents were more a borderline adult than YA and I liked that! <br><br><b>"I want to touch you.".."I want to feel what's mine.Whta's always been mine."</b><br><b>“Are you mine?” I asked as I wiped my tears.<br>He kissed the corners of my mouth softly, and I felt heat rise up my neck. “Always have been,”<br>he whispered against my mouth."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426399ra/852021.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Jared and Tate:<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426399i/852022._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426399i/852023.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><br><br>For more reviews you can check mine and Kristinas's blog. :D<br><br> <a href="http://readmore-sleepless.blogspot.gr/" rel="nofollow noopener">my link text</a><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380387651i/747742.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> </span>

<div id="review_1011965013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011965013" />
    <a title="Ramona Popescu " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33526516-ramona-popescu"><img alt="Ramona Popescu " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594649997p2/33526516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011965013?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramona Popescu " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramona Popescu " href="/user/show/33526516-ramona-popescu">Ramona Popescu </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33526516-ramona-popescu?shelf=hot-romance">hot-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33526516-ramona-popescu?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33526516-ramona-popescu?shelf=love-this-series">love-this-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011965013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14620476338816873519">When I think about how I've started reading contemporary romance, the first book that pops in my head is Bully. I was fascinated by a lot of elements, mostly the striking way in which the love scenes were described, but the list can go on forever and ever. <br/><br/>Now looking back after reading around 300 books, I think that "Bully" is unique in plot and in theme provided. There weren't a lot of books that had this approach, making you question the morality of the characters and really raising awareness</span>
  <span id="freeText14620476338816873519" style="display:none">When I think about how I've started reading contemporary romance, the first book that pops in my head is Bully. I was fascinated by a lot of elements, mostly the striking way in which the love scenes were described, but the list can go on forever and ever. <br><br>Now looking back after reading around 300 books, I think that "Bully" is unique in plot and in theme provided. There weren't a lot of books that had this approach, making you question the morality of the characters and really raising awareness for a difficult problem. <br><br>"Bully" was intense from page one and managed to catch my attention immediately. The story between Tate and Jared is one of a kind and when you drawn the line, it is very confusing to choose sides. Let me explain more in detail:<br>Tate and Jared were close, super close and had a wonderful friendship. Tate loved Jared, but was afraid to tell him that, because he was super popular and she wasn't confident enough to share that with him. It is all pink with ribbons until Jared goes to stay with his dad for the summer holiday and comes back different but in an ugly way. After that, he becomes Tate's bully, harassing her with every chance he got, and believe me it was not pretty. <br>This book confused me so much, because of the mixed feeling it generated. You want them to be together, but in the same time you want Tate to kick him in his manly parts and move on.<br><br>On the first hand, I would of want Tate to fight harder and not to forget easily the way Jared treated her. He brought down her confidence and self esteem and she should have made him work harder for her love and forgiveness. If I were to think better, she is very admirable for managing to forgive him, because what he did was not ok. She had to go to France to get away from him:)<br><br>Jared on the other hand was very tormented and conflicted, that went through a traumatic experience, but nobody deserved to be treated this way because of it. He blamed Tate for his past, but he was so wrong. Maybe he felt stronger, wiser and could forget what happened then, but in the end I don't think either of those things work. The pain still remains and he inflicted it on a person that loved him so much.<br><br>So, I am confused. I loved them as a couple and for their endless sexual chemistry and intensity, but on the other hand, maybe it was better for them to be apart, because I just can't understand how you can love somebody that damages you so badly. But I know, in the end you can forgive and move on when you truly believe that person is sorry. I know, but it is not fare.. She was too king and carrying and sweet to put up with all his baggage and stuff. <br><br>I can write an essay for this book, but for me is still special, an example of love and hate towards the hero, because he is my main target. I didn't managed to completely love Jared, because I am a person who can't forget depending on the damaged made. Lucky for him Tate did:)<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479123324i/21149668._SX540_.png" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more reviews please check <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readwithloveblog.wordpress.com">https://readwithloveblog.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14620476338816873519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_646807294" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646807294" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646807294?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=quick-read">quick-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=dropped-series">dropped-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646807294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2376491634346170086"><b>Initial thoughts:</b> Not worth the time taken to read. I honestly thought it would be a better read than it actually was - it wasn't terrible in the beginning, but at the same time, as it went on, it glorifies and romanticizes bullying to no end. I have a lot of words to say about this and I'll try to be as constructive as I can about what went wrong with this read after I meditate a bit over it.<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>This is a difficult review for me to write, but I'm going to start this reflection with a fe</span>
  <span id="freeText2376491634346170086" style="display:none"><b>Initial thoughts:</b> Not worth the time taken to read. I honestly thought it would be a better read than it actually was - it wasn't terrible in the beginning, but at the same time, as it went on, it glorifies and romanticizes bullying to no end. I have a lot of words to say about this and I'll try to be as constructive as I can about what went wrong with this read after I meditate a bit over it.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />This is a difficult review for me to write, but I'm going to start this reflection with a few thoughts about current trends I see in popular literature. I think it's fair to say that conflict drives much of what we read and the experiences that we get from that conflict in a work make us value it in a myriad of ways. But one thing that I absolutely loathe that I see on the rise is the fetishization (not sure if that's a word) of problems at their deepest roots, that entail suffering without context for what it is or having any moral consequences. I've read stories where rape is glorified, where abuse - physical, mental, emotional - is championed and desired over respect in a relationship, and in the case of Penelope Douglas's "Bully", bullying is seen as something that's desirable despite of a victim's experiences.<br /><br />I'm not going to take away from Douglas's narrative in the fact that it is compulsively readable and that it starts off with a heroine that does stand up for herself in the face of torments that she endures from the people who surround her. "Bully" had me, I went along with the story for a while. But then it lost me as it became clear that in all the measures surrounding this story, it glorifies falling in love with someone who torments you. Regardless of whatever issues the hero had, it doesn't justify what he did to Tate, and I sincerely doubt after all that Jared did, Tate could forgive and lust after him as easily as she did.<br /><br />Tate (Tatum) is a young woman who returns to town for her senior year after being away for a year in France. Her father is out on business, leaving Tatum by her lonesome at home, with a grandmother who occasionally checks in on her (though that was a little hard to believe, I suspended my disbelief enough to follow the story). Tate was once friends with her next door neighbor, Jared, but after he returned home after a stay with his father, he started to bully her. Some turns of his bullying is horrific to say the least, alongside his friends and jealous girlfriends who join into making Tate's life miserable when she returns to town. Still, I liked how Tate stood up for herself in spells, and her retorts in places were actually humored well. I don't know how I felt about the monologue - I know some people would think it's emotionally resonant, but for me, for all the considerations of what Tate went through, it didn't hit me as hard as I would've liked.<br /><br />After a point, it was obvious that Tate was championed as having a love/hate relationship with Jared despite the horrible things he said and did to her. I hated that because there's a line between the whole "I love you/I hate you" dynamic and having a hero who obviously gets off on hurting others while the heroine still succumbs to lust in light of that. This actually could've been a narrative where it clearly established Tate lusted after the boy that Jared used to be, but that measure was lost in the foray of the current actions that Jared did to her. <br /><br />I still think one of the few authors who managed to portray a hero who was a jerk but was truly repentant of his ways and manages to be likable in turns was Kody Keplinger. Granted, "The DUFF" is YA, and this is NA, but at the same time - that felt more real of a story than this one and truly had something to say about its characters and the issues/conflicts it presented. "Bully" was shallow, underdeveloped, and fetishizing a major social and societal problem in comparison.<br /><br />It forces the point home when Tate is a victim in so many ways and shouldn't have had to endure it, especially with other people in her circles simply dismissing Jared's actions so casually and them telling her in so many words "give him a chance". Eff NO. Yes, it's true that in order to understand the root of bullying and bullying behaviors, you have to see what factors play into the behaviors that are displayed and come to an understanding about why the bully engages the victim in the way they do. Usually that comes with getting help and having the bully deal with with what's perpetuating those behaviors in proper context. But to come at the expense of the victim and in not so subtle terms put the responsibility on the "victim" to change the "bully"? No, just no. I don't care what age group this book is intended for, that's not a good attitude to approach the matter.<br /><br />Even when Tate figures that K.C. goes out with Jared for a time, I found it hard to believe Tate would turn a blind eye or feel guilty for distancing herself from a friend who would do that. Granted, I know the lot of us have different coping points and thresholds for forgiveness, but this narrative asked me one too many times to overlook some jarring conflicts in an attempt to see how the leading love interests "get together." It was milked and manufactured and I did not see the constructiveness of its portrayal here.<br /><br />Overall, I was very disappointed with the narrative here and I couldn't get behind the relationship or the insinuations made on the subject matter here. It's drama for the sake of drama, with characters that I'm supposed to believe fall in love, but it didn't progress with any kind of realistic terms for me to believe in it.<br /><br />Overall score: 1/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="2376491634346170086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/647937195?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lisa •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lisa •" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa">• Lisa •</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647937195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7845378525243156480">4 FALLING IN LOVE STARS.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"I want to touch you, I want to feel what's mine. What's always been mine."</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426326i/851784._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What's it all about?<br/>Two former friends Jared Trent and Tate Brandt now find themselves as mortal enemies. After years of being inseparable the duo find themselves in the ultimate love/hate relationship. Tate has suffered for years at the hands of Jared's constant taunting and pranks so after a year away in Europe Tate returns to Shelburne falls high school determined to be stronger. In a stando</span>
  <span id="freeText7845378525243156480" style="display:none">4 FALLING IN LOVE STARS.<br><br><i>
  <b>"I want to touch you, I want to feel what's mine. What's always been mine."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426326i/851784._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What's it all about?<br>Two former friends Jared Trent and Tate Brandt now find themselves as mortal enemies. After years of being inseparable the duo find themselves in the ultimate love/hate relationship. Tate has suffered for years at the hands of Jared's constant taunting and pranks so after a year away in Europe Tate returns to Shelburne falls high school determined to be stronger. In a standoff between hate, lust, secret reveals and broken hearts what will become of a friendship that was and a hate filled relationship that may have run it's course.<br><br>Meet the characters ...<br>Jared is troubled and angry at the world for his past. He is handsome with a streak of mean, if you've got a thing for a bad boy with a sad past then Jared will hit the mark for you.<br><br>Tate is essentially a good girl gone a little astray, throughout the story she  has conflicting behaviours, on one side shes the studious all round high school brain, on the flip side she's the ball buster, a girl who is not afraid to stand up for herself after years of hiding away.<br><br>What I liked/loved ...<br>The author has created an easy reading style, which makes for a lighthearted reading experience. The story has all the makings for a usual over dramatised young adult story which has angst written all over it giving the story extra interest and intrigue. We are also given a plot that delivers a bit of everything, a taste of mean girls and bad boys, sexual tension, and a surprising amount of heat for a YA storyline. <br><br>Final thoughts ...<br>If you love YA then you will no doubt enjoy this story, it is on the immature side of that genre so steer clear if that isn't for you. All in all an enjoyable escape into the pre adult world of high school drama and falling in love. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426326i/851785._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4 STARS.</span>

<div id="review_1305330732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305330732" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1305330732?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Katerina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/37314676-nicoleta-e-addicted-to-books">NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305330732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7397871229193412754">I didn't want light and sweet romance.I needed <b>angst</b> and <b>pain</b> and <b>tears</b> and <b>fights</b> and all kinds of <b>feelings</b>.<br/>And I found them all in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20803953.Bully__Fall_Away___1_' title='Bully (Fall Away, #1) by Penelope Douglas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bully</a>.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This is how bullies are made.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>How bullies are made?Is there a reason for their behavior and the pleasure they find in physically and emotionally abusing innocent people?Do they feel a surge of power when they belittle others?I can't say I was a popular girl in school (you see,I was the geek,the perfect student and that didn't exactly make me Miss</span>
  <span id="freeText7397871229193412754" style="display:none">I didn't want light and sweet romance.I needed <b>angst</b> and <b>pain</b> and <b>tears</b> and <b>fights</b> and all kinds of <b>feelings</b>.<br>And I found them all in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20803953.Bully__Fall_Away___1_" title="Bully (Fall Away, #1) by Penelope Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Bully</a>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This is how bullies are made.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>How bullies are made?Is there a reason for their behavior and the pleasure they find in physically and emotionally abusing innocent people?Do they feel a surge of power when they belittle others?I can't say I was a popular girl in school (you see,I was the geek,the perfect student and that didn't exactly make me Miss Congeniality) but the discomfort I sometimes felt was nothing compared to the things Tate went through in Bully.And what I learned while reading this book,was that when bullies see weakness,it makes them even more hungry.When they see tears once,they crave more.Ignoring them or fighting them are the only options to survive.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Isn’t it about time you fought back?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What happens though when in the urge to fight you become like them?Bully follows Tate and Jared's story.They were childhood friends,until after spending one summer away Jared became Tate's worst enemy.At first she let him get to her,she suffered and did nothing about it until she decided enough was enough.And that's when things got complicated.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Actually I am,after reading the first pages and witnessed the way Jared treated Tate,I couldn't imagine why she would ever want to be with him and what reason was enough to justify his actions.And it took me a while to forgive and trust Jared,but I ended up irrevocably in love with him.And with the story.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402461ra/782291.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <u>The reasons I loved Bully</u>
</b><br>-The <b>music</b>.Avenged Sevenfold,Papa Roach,Apocalyptica,Bullet for My Valentine?I just went to metal heaven!<br>-The <b>feelings</b>.No kidding,it was an emotional rollercoaster.The fury and the sadness over the injustice of the situation were overwhelming,but I could also feel giddy and fuzzy and the butterflies were dancing paso doble in my stomach!<br>-The line seperating abuser from victim was fine and blurry.There was plenty food for thought and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7139136.Penelope_Douglas" title="Penelope Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Penelope Douglas</a> painted vividly,without holding back,how cruel teenagers can be and how easy it is to cross the line and the war that rages inside you when you do.<br>-Just the perfect amount of drama.<br>-The <b>sexual tension</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442919801ra/16294051.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Enough said.<br>-The <b>romance</b>.Besides the hot and heavy make out sessions (and more) there was also love,the love between two kids that found in the other a safe haven,a lantern to guide them back to light.And even though Jared broke Tate's trust and heart,he could put them back together.<br>-<b>Jared</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421443092ra/13377023.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you have any doubts about reading this book,just ignore them.You are going to love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7397871229193412754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2459374180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2459374180" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2459374180?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2459374180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16118851896464271831">ATTENTION ❗️<i> nearly-rape, child-abuse, alcoholism, bullying </i> <br/><br/><i> “I like storms. <br/>Thunder torrential rain, puddles, wet shoes. <br/>When the clouds roll in, I get filled with this giddy expectation. <br/>Everything is more beautiful in the rain. <br/>Don't ask me why. <br/>But it’s like this whole other realm of opportunity.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>Tates life is a living hell. Jared, her former best friend, is bullying her and making her school life miserable. But after one year gone she’s not the vulnerable weak girl anymore.</span>
  <span id="freeText16118851896464271831" style="display:none">ATTENTION ❗️<i> nearly-rape, child-abuse, alcoholism, bullying </i> <br /><br /><i> “I like storms. <br />Thunder torrential rain, puddles, wet shoes. <br />When the clouds roll in, I get filled with this giddy expectation. <br />Everything is more beautiful in the rain. <br />Don't ask me why. <br />But it’s like this whole other realm of opportunity.” </i> <br /><br />Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Tates life is a living hell. Jared, her former best friend, is bullying her and making her school life miserable. But after one year gone she’s not the vulnerable weak girl anymore. Now she pushes back and finally she sees something more than Jareds hatred.<br />But after all these years of pain and anger is there really a way to see Jared as her former best friend and accept the feelings that’s in the air? <br />Im not really sure if I liked the story or not, but the fact that I read this book in one day should be a great factor. But I had some problems with the whole bad boy trope involving bullying and all. I love bad boys, don’t get me wrong, I’m a sucker for pained villains, but not the type that treat the girl like shit and tells her “that he doesn’t care if she’s alive or dead”. Yeah, I don’t care how cute he is in the end. That shit is just unforgivable. Sorry not sorry. Deal with it. <br />TREAT YOUR PARTNER/LOVE LIKE YOU WANT TO BE TREATED! 👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻<br /><br />Character ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><i> “Being a bitch could be a survival technique. <br />They get respect.” </i> <br />I wasn’t so sure about my feelings for Tate. I mean I loved her when she shut down stupid comments with her sassy mouth, but the way she acted around Jared was so... ugh, I don’t know. Maybe I can’t really relate because my male best friends in my childhood were the nicest and treated me well. <br />But still, I liked her a little bit. <br />Then Jared. I mean, I do get why Tate was so attracted to him. But the way he treated her was just a major no go. <br />And I don’t care what happened in his childhood or blabla. For me these are low and poor excuses for such a horrible way of treating others. <br />Sure, he’s handsome and drives great cars. But I would choose a person with a wonderful character over and over again. <br />I get that our past shouldn’t hound us forever, but you should be really remorse about things you do and in a time space of more than one year you should realize that when a girl cries, she’s hurt? Idiot. <br />Sorry not sorry. <br />You ask yourself - why does she give “characters” four stars? Because I felt something for the characters. I felt hate, or pity or I was sad and a little bit happy. <br />But I felt something. <br /><br />Relationships ⭐️⭐️<br /><i> “You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. <br />I loved all those things, and I loved you.” </i> <br />First of all I’m a sucker for the childhood-best-friend-plot. Can’t blame me for that. I wanted a cute neighbor who watches rains and storms with me. But no, only boring old people. <br />But then I’m also extremely unforgiving. <br />If you’re ever disrespectful or mean to me, I’m probably gonna hate you until you die. <br />I mean I can forgive, but not meanness or cruelty and especially not bullying. <br />Yeah, I know this was the whole bad boy trope, but still. Not my style of relationship. Definitely not. <br /><br />Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Hm, im not really sure about that one either. First of all it was definitely addictive, no way of denying that. But the writing wasn’t special or brilliantly steamy or something like that. It was nice, it was enjoyable and it was written in just one POV - Tate.<br />I did love one part of the story - Tate’s monologue. It was so beautiful and breathtaking. My heart was pounding like crazy and I was happy and sad at the same time. <br />All in all it was really entertaining and I’m glad I read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16118851896464271831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1790500325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1790500325" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1790500325?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20871378-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51318038-elena?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1790500325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16204270465822625699"><blockquote>
  <i>❝There was a time when I had all of his attention and loved it. As much as I wanted him to leave me alone, I also liked how he seemed surprised. I liked the way he was looking at me right now. And then I remembered that I hated him.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Bully</i> wasn't really that enjoyable. It was filled with too much drama, annoying characters that deserve to be punched in the face, and wasted time. It was enjoyable when Jared changed, but the beginning of it was boring and not interesting. I've never heard of th</span>
  <span id="freeText16204270465822625699" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝There was a time when I had all of his attention and loved it. As much as I wanted him to leave me alone, I also liked how he seemed surprised. I liked the way he was looking at me right now. And then I remembered that I hated him.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Bully</i> wasn't really that enjoyable. It was filled with too much drama, annoying characters that deserve to be punched in the face, and wasted time. It was enjoyable when Jared changed, but the beginning of it was boring and not interesting. I've never heard of this author and her books, and I don't really want to continue the series only because I know it involves a lot of characters I actually didn't like. Even though there are news ones to be introduced, they're only gonna end up getting together with these recurring characters and it's gonna make me roll my eyes more.<br /><br />To summarize the novel, <i>Bully</i> is about Tate, the full name is actually Tatum, who is basically missing her old best friend and wondering why he hates her so much. Tate and Jared have been best friends since they were children. As Jared told her, he literally wanted to become her friend when he first saw her when she moved in next to him with her dad because she was the only hope he actually had. As time passed by and Jared and Tate become close friends where they sleepover at each other's house, climb trees and tell each other secrets, and just be those young kids that try their best to have fun and live, there isn't really anything separating them two. They rely on each other and both are able to comfort the other when it is needed. <br /><br />But when Jared returns from visiting his father, Jared isn't the same Jared Trent she met when they were little. <b>Why?</b> Who knows. Before freshman year, Jared started bullying Tate <b>for no reason</b>. He tried making her life a living hell. Literally. He spread rumors about her, tried making her high school year miserable, wanted her to shed tears because of him. Tate decides to go to Europe and forget about Jared for a while. Not completely forget about him, but to get her mind refreshed and set up. When she returns, she isn't the same Tate anymore. She's stronger and isn't up for any of the lies Jared has to make and will make. She'll face him and anything he comes up with. But what Tate doesn't know is that it won't be that easy and simple to stand up to Jared.<br /><br /><i>Bully</i> wasn't all that good if I'm being honest. I hated how Tate told herself that she hated Jared and she wanted nothing to do with him <i>when she really did.</i> She kept telling herself that Jared can't get to her but as she would try and push him away, she failed. Sure, she was able to stand up to him and tell him off, but that was because "she changed" and that was what I didn't like. Jared bullied her for a reason, and she suddenly returns from a trip and is this totally different girl. I found it stupid how she tried to stand up to him but couldn't only because she missed him and didn't admit it. If she really wanted him out of her life and didn't want to do anything that had to do with him, she would've. But when she pushed him away, she tried pulling him back and that also lead to him telling her the truth and suddenly the two are in love and everything is okay. <b>Nothing was okay.</b> I just hated how she wanted to be with him and actually forgave him when all he did was stupid things and treated her like shit. She was all over him and would forget about the things he did to her just because she was so in love with him and literally up on him. <i>Stupid dreamy looks.</i><br /><br />Jared was an asshole at first, but I was glad he told her the truth and the whole truth. Still, I didn't accept him and who he was. His stories and lies didn't make up for it and his excuses just made everything worse. He really didn't have a reason to bully Tate because Tate didn't even do anything and doesn't even know what she did to deserve this. Even though Jared told her the truth and told her the reason for her bullying him, it was still stupid. Sure, there were reasons behind everything he said and did to her, but it still was dumb. Coming back from visiting his father is no excuse to treat a childhood friend like he did. Here's the thing: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>He went to visit his father. He abused him and his brother. Jared came back home. Jared treats Tate like shit before Freshman year when Tate did nothing.</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He would also say he needed Tate but then the next day, he'd be calling her whatever he wanted to call her and nothing else would happen. There was just no chemistry between the two and I just wished they would stay as friends instead. Honestly, who the fuck does Jared think he is deciding to turn his back on his childhood friend and once-best friend without telling her what she did wrong? <b>It just didn't make sense!</b><br /><br />Another thing I hated about Tate is how she shouldn't have cared who Jared was with but she did. She cared who was with him and who he was with. She would tell herself she hated him but in reality, it hurt her inside. There was never a hint of romance when they were children, and there was nothing else besides friendship. She'd be mad at her friend because she was all up on Jared and it was just stupid because she pretended to care. Sure, her best friend is stupid because she knew/knows that Jared has hurt Tate so many times and keep ignoring her, pushing her away, making her life even more of a living hell yet her best friend, K.C., kept being all up on Jared and even lied to Tate about it. Sure, that was annoying as hell and I hated her for it because she is her best friend for a reason yet she's over her childhood friend instead of comforting her and making her feel better, but Tate had no reason to tell her about her lies and how stupid it is for her to not realize that Jared is using her. What did she care anyway? I thought she hated Jared and didn't care about anything he did anymore? <i>Tate had no chill many times throughout the whole book.</i><br /><br />I hated the romance and didn't like it only because of who Tate and Jared were. I don't even know if Jared liked her like he said he did when they were practically strangers, but I know Tate did and she couldn't even get a hold of herself. It didn't make sense to me and it just reminded me a little of <i>Swear on this Life</i> how they were childhood friends, strangers at one point, and then suddenly fall for each other again and don't want to let go of each other. It was all just dumb. I only kept reading this to find out the reason why Jared was an asshole to her at first and see what his excuses were.<br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed Jared's character a lot more than Tate and anyone else. I didn't like the other characters because Tate's best friend was a betraying hoe, and Jared's friends were horny dicks that couldn't keep their hands to themselves and just wanted to make Jared mad and jealous. I didn't enjoy this like at all. Romance is the main thing in this and I actually hated it. It didn't feel real and their connections felt off and fake, I couldn't care a bit. I didn't have any expectations for this since only a couple of my friends enjoyed this one and the rest are just negative thoughts, opinions, and reviews. I read most of them without spoiling myself and honestly, I wish I was spoiled that way I wouldn't have bothered buying this and actually reading it. The whole plot was just cringe, boring, and so unrealistic. This is also, probably, surely, the worst NA novel I've read <b>this year.</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16204270465822625699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_646557095" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646557095" />
    <a title="Jen " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5962787-jen"><img alt="Jen " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563496869p2/5962787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646557095?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen " href="/user/show/5962787-jen">Jen </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=good-girl-meets-bad-boy">good-girl-meets-bad-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=friends-to-luvahs">friends-to-luvahs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646557095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11002720502514734848"><b>
  <i>”You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all of those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>For 3 years Jared has been making Tate’s life a living hell. He taunts her at every turn, makes up nasty stories about her and threatens any guy that even tries to get close to her. The kicker? Tate and Jared were once the best of frie</span>
  <span id="freeText11002720502514734848" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all of those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</i>
</b><br /><br />For 3 years Jared has been making Tate’s life a living hell. He taunts her at every turn, makes up nasty stories about her and threatens any guy that even tries to get close to her. The kicker? Tate and Jared were once the best of friends and Tate has no idea what she did to piss Jared off. Up until their senior year, Jared’s ruined any chance Tate has had at a normal high school existence and girlfriend is <b>DONE!</b><br /><br />I definitely enjoyed this book. The story’s told from Tate’s POV and we really get to see how much Jared’s bullying has messed with her life. Academically she excels but socially she’s completely unsure of herself. The wonderful thing is that she’s in no way unsure of herself as a person and she knows exactly what she’s worth. To see her finally stand up and start taking charge was absolutely awesome!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Don’t touch me and don’t talk to me.” I hovered over him, sneering. Madoc’s eyes were closed as he breathed hard. “Did you really think I would go out with you? I hear the girls talk, and contrary to popular belief, good things do not come in small packages.”</i>
</b> <br /><br />There’s nothing more entertaining than seeing a formally abused girl turn the tables and knee a jackass, in this case Jared’s best friend, in the balls. I could read that shit for days! While Tate had me from the beginning, it took me a <i>long</i> time to warm up to Jared. At about the fifty percent mark we start to see chinks in the armor he’s erected around himself and he finally starts to actually show signs that there might be a decent human being lurking under all of that animosity. It’s obvious from the beginning he harbors some deep feelings for Tate and when he finally, after much coaxing, lets Tate in it’s a beautiful thing. <br /><br />As much as I loved this book, I still had some issues. This poor girl was bullied for years by a popular boy and everyone just fell in line with it, no questions asked. She’s beautiful and smart and at some point I would hope a few brave souls, excluding her one best friend, would question why she was being turned into a social pariah. At times she was physically grabbed by Jared’s cronies and no one seemed to give a shit. And no one seemed to question Jared's relentless pursuit in making her life a living hell. I also didn’t fully buy Jared’s reasoning for the bullying. If he truly loved her to the extent he said he did, he would never have made her as miserable as he did and then be SURPRISED about the fact she didn't trust him. Although I loved reading this from Tate's POV, a chapter or two from Jared's perspective might've helped me understand his character and his hurtful actions more.<br /><br />Bottom line, this is a really fantastic book. I’m already looking forward to Madoc’s tale and considering he was asshole number 2 in this story, I think that says something about the great writing that went into creating this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11002720502514734848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_812437103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/812437103" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/812437103?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18103090-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer812437103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10863496055166983442">Gah, another tough one to review. I don't understand quite a few things that occurred. Really. And I consider myself a fairly intelligent person. A lot of this just didn't make any logical sense. <br/><br/>Jared and Tate used to be besties. The summer of their 14th year, Jared goes to stay with his father for a few weeks and comes home different. Now he hates Tate. When the book begins, they're both 16, and Jared has spent two years bullying Tate. He's also enlisted the help of his friend, Madoc. No one r</span>
  <span id="freeText10863496055166983442" style="display:none">Gah, another tough one to review. I don't understand quite a few things that occurred. Really. And I consider myself a fairly intelligent person. A lot of this just didn't make any logical sense. <br /><br />Jared and Tate used to be besties. The summer of their 14th year, Jared goes to stay with his father for a few weeks and comes home different. Now he hates Tate. When the book begins, they're both 16, and Jared has spent two years bullying Tate. He's also enlisted the help of his friend, Madoc. No one really knows why Jared hates Tate, not even Tate herself. She's meek, weak, confused, sad, etc. Then she goes away to study in France for a year. When she comes home, she makes the decision that Jared isn't going to take her senior year away from her, so she begins to fight back. And here's where the hilarity ensues. <br /><br />Only not really. None of this is funny. It's confusing and taxing and cruel. I give the author props for the way she wove some serious angst into this tale, but so much of it was just completely unnecessary. I understand how things could turn out this way <i>if</i> the people involved chose to act the way these characters did. But I just can't see real people acting that way. If my best friend of four years suddenly started bullying me with no obvious reason, you can bet your ass I wouldn't quit hounding him until I got some answers. Tate just...well, she apparently just gave up. It was like Jared said a few mean things to her and she stood there confused, then just shrugged and said, "Well, whatever" and accepted the new situation. And she wondered why Jared thought she was a self-serving bitch? <br /><br />You know, I was going to say that it seemed like one of them deserved better, but now I think they really did deserve each other. In all their emotionally stunted glory. <br /><br />Why did no one ever get Jared psychological help? Dude went through a lot, and no one thought it prudent for him to see a counselor? K.<br /><br />I just...wanted to love this. I really, really did. It was just a wee bit over the top for my taste. Especially toward the end when things start really spiraling out of control what with a sex tape and everything. It was like a teen drama on MTV or something. <br /><br />Oh, and let's not forget K.C. Dear me, how could I forget? If one of my friends started dating a guy who'd bullied me for three years and basically told me I just had to deal with it....yeah.<br /><br />Last but not least, I am <i>sick to death</i> of the way female sexuality is being portrayed in books like this. The girls who have sex are "slutty" and/or "not nice girls". Most of the sexually active females in this book are evil. Jared ends up being Tate's first, and that's oh-so-romantic since they've loved each other since they were kids....but it was perfectly all right for <i>Jared</i> to be out screwing everyone and their dogs beforehand? <br /><br />Sheesh. I disliked this book more than I thought. <br /><br />Even for all that, I thought the message was....no. I don't know what I thought. This book confused me, and for that, I can't forgive it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10863496055166983442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9464268611689211333">Holy shite... I L.O.V.E.D. it!!!<br/>I mean, I loved it hard.<br/>I could not put it down.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502887704ra/23607119.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>*the GIF above is representative of my excitement for this 5 star read upon my completion of it at 3am. <br/><br/>Who's a sucker for complete alphaholes?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488654430ra/22141176.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Jared is a complete and total alphahole. </b> the big jerk. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502889044ra/23607411.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can take it. I'll just be sitting here blissfully reliving all the yummy feels this book gave me. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502889044ra/23607412.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030647668?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lo Bookfrantic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lo Bookfrantic" href="/user/show/14746493-lo-bookfrantic">Lo Bookfrantic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14746493-lo-bookfrantic?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14746493-lo-bookfrantic?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14746493-lo-bookfrantic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030647668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6709665756500003128"><p>
  
    <strong>4.5★★★★Stars</strong>
  
</p><br/><strong>Genre: </strong><em>YA</em><strong>-</strong><em>Contemporary Romance</em> <br/> <strong>Type: </strong><em>Standalone Book 1 of Fall Away Series</em><br/> <strong>POV: </strong><em>First Person – Female</em><br/><br/><p>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498685013i/23152113._SX540_.jpg' alt='teaser 2 6-28-17' width='500' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <em> </em>
  <br/>
</p><blockquote>
  
    <strong>
      <em>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</em>
    </strong>
  
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498685013ra/23152114.gif' width='500' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong>
  Tatum "Tate" Brandt has been bullied by one person in particular her entire</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText6709665756500003128" style="display:none"><p>
  
    <strong>4.5★★★★Stars</strong>
  
</p><br><strong>Genre: </strong><em>YA</em><strong>-</strong><em>Contemporary Romance</em> <br> <strong>Type: </strong><em>Standalone Book 1 of Fall Away Series</em><br> <strong>POV: </strong><em>First Person – Female</em><br><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498685013i/23152113._SX540_.jpg" alt="teaser 2 6-28-17" width="500" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <em> </em>
  <br>
</p><blockquote>
  
    <strong>
      <em>“You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</em>
    </strong>
  
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498685013ra/23152114.gif" width="500" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>
  Tatum "Tate" Brandt has been bullied by one person in particular her entire high school years.  She was easily intimidated by him aka Jared.  Jared was once her best friend until he wasn't; and she couldn't understand why in the world he would be so mean to her.
</strong><br><br><blockquote>
  
    <strong>
      <em>"Thanks to Jared, my high school experience had been one long succession of rumors, pranks, tears, and disappointments."</em>
    </strong>
  
</blockquote><br><br><strong>
  Jared Trent was the popular boy in high school.  Everyone wanted to be him or be with him.  The girls melted over him.  Jared had bad boy written all over him.  He loved to race cars and was a complete mystery to me.  Something dramatic happened to him when he was fourteen years old and I am a sucker for damaged boys I desperately wanted to know more.
</strong><br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    
      <em>"Jared indulged in my misery like it was candy. He had fed me to the wolves time and again, reveling in the unhappiness he caused. Jared, my friend, was completely gone, leaving a cold monster in his place."</em>
    
  </strong>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498685013ra/23152115.gif" width="500" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><em> </em><strong>
  I have wanted to read this book for such a very long time.  I don't know why I waited so long because this story was so good.  From the very first page the book grabbed my attention and I just wanted to know how this would end.  At first I will be honest I had mixed feelings for Jared.  He made me frustrated and I usually like assholes but he was up high up on a new level of assholes but I still found myself desperate for answers to know why he was such an ass.
</strong><br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    
      <em>"His eyes were like the cover of a book- giving you hints but not the whole story. And I wanted to know the story."</em>
    
  </strong>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>
  The tension buildup between Tate and Jared was intense I loved every second of it. It totally may me melt for him more haha.  I had mixed feeling about Tate as well. Like the insecure shy part of her drove me mad until she finally decided to stand up for herself; I like that personality much better. I felt like the anger and the heat buildup created for an excellent sexy read and made a much intense relationship.
</strong><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498685013i/23152116._SX540_.jpg" alt="teaser 1 6-28-17" width="500" height="430" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><p></p><br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>"His mouth crashed down on mine, drowning out my protest. His lips devoured me, hard and fast, like I was being eaten alive."</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498685013ra/23152117.gif" width="500" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>
  Overall, I enjoyed this story a lot.  The chemistry, the tension, the drama, everything was exciting and the author did a wonderful job creating a unique story that I won't be forgetting anytime soon. I feel that readers who enjoy broken heroes, young adult drama and second chances will truly like this story.
</strong><br><br><blockquote>
  
    <em>
      <strong> “Yesterday lasts forever. Tomorrow comes never. Until you” </strong>
    </em>
  
</blockquote><br><br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498685013ra/23152118.gif" width="500" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_647145775" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/647145775" />
    <a title="Geri Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads"><img alt="Geri Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487874758p2/11757728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/647145775?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geri Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geri Reads" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads">Geri Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647145775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2740626031360305965"><b>4.5 surprising stars</b><br/><br/>Wow! This book really took me by surprise. I haven't read YA in a while but this was a freebie on Amazon right now, so I one-clicked it. I was intrigued by the premise and at the same time cautious because the bullying thing might be too much for me to handle. But I ended up really, really liking it. <br/><br/><b>What I liked</b><br/><br/>- I loved the writing. It has great dialogue and really well developed characters. The story didn't lag. There were no wasted dialogue or purple prose which seems to </span>
  <span id="freeText2740626031360305965" style="display:none"><b>4.5 surprising stars</b><br /><br />Wow! This book really took me by surprise. I haven't read YA in a while but this was a freebie on Amazon right now, so I one-clicked it. I was intrigued by the premise and at the same time cautious because the bullying thing might be too much for me to handle. But I ended up really, really liking it. <br /><br /><b>What I liked</b><br /><br />- I loved the writing. It has great dialogue and really well developed characters. The story didn't lag. There were no wasted dialogue or purple prose which seems to be common in this genre. Very well written. <br /><br />- The characters, Tate and Jared. I loved them, Tate especially. She was a tough cookie and I loved it when she finally fought back. That was the best part of the book for me. I also personally connected with them. Now, I didn't always agree with their choices, (Yes, I'm talking about you, Jared) but that doesn't mean I couldn't relate to them. <br /><br />- The plot. I thought the bully thing would offend me especially since it seems like the heroine, who was bullied, had the thing for her bully. But then I realized that they were actually friends before, and may or may have feelings for each other before they had a falling out. Their falling out was dealt with as the story progressed. And we get to see Jared side of the story. His explanation seems shallow at first but after I thought about it and putting into consideration what happened to him at the hands of his father, I could totally understand his reasoning. Again, not saying I agree with it but he was 14 or 15 when these changes occurred and by the time he was 18, he just fell into the pattern of making her life miserable.<br /><br />Bullying is such a sensitive topic right now, so I will let each reader judge for themselves but it's safe to say there was no physical bullying involved or anything like that. The bullying was more like in the vein of telling a guy who wanted to date her she had lice so he won't ask her out or something like that. But of this was set in high school, so rumor like that would totally make you a social leper. So Tate did suffer because of that. I did feel that Jared redeemed himself at the end, and what made his actions a little easier to understand was the fact that he was never a school bully per se. He didn't bully other kids. It was just Tate, which makes the reader wonder if there was more to it. <br /><br />- Loved that monologue that Tate delivered in front of the class with Jared listening. Loved it. I cried with her. And Jared's reaction. Wow! <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>“Everything still hurts, but I know none of it is my fault. There are a lot of words that I could use to describe you, but the only one that includes sad, angry, miserable, and pitiful is “coward.” In a year, I’ll be gone, and you’ll be nothing but some washout whose height of existence was in high school.” My eyes were still on Jared, and my voice got strong again. The ache in my face from trying to hold back tears eased. “You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.”</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />- The steam level. Again, this was YA, so I wasn't expecting any steam at all. But this one was surprisingly steamy. There were a couple of hot scenes and very hot dream sequence which are NSFW material. It fit with the characters though, so totally on board with the steam. :D<br /><br />This is definitely one of the better YAs out there and if you can stomach YA or the sensitive topic, then this book will definitely work for you. Enjoy!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2740626031360305965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
