<div id="review_645785172" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645785172" />
    <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog"><img alt="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429608146p2/12994342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645785172?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog">Smitten&#39;s Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18090508-bully">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=angst-filled-reads">angst-filled-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=bad-boy">bad-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=domestic-child-abuse">domestic-child-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=steamy-reads">steamy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=amazing-sexual-tension">amazing-sexual-tension</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=hea">hea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=men-with-ink">men-with-ink</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=college-romance">college-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645785172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17018838186580133"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850775._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850776._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>This is how bullies are made.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Squeeeeeee!!! Freakin' awesome!<br/><br/>I absolutely love love loved this book. This is the definition of a hate-to-love story and it totally rocked. I could not put it down. <br/><br/>I was really craving a book that would make me stop everything I was supposed to be doing and devour every word... and that's exactly what <i>Bully</i> did!<br/><br/>I'd heard the hype about this book and seen lots of my book buddies giving it great reviews and five stars, so I knew I had to give a shot asap.</span>
  <span id="freeText17018838186580133" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850775._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850776._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>This is how bullies are made.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Squeeeeeee!!! Freakin' awesome!<br><br>I absolutely love love loved this book. This is the definition of a hate-to-love story and it totally rocked. I could not put it down. <br><br>I was really craving a book that would make me stop everything I was supposed to be doing and devour every word... and that's exactly what <i>Bully</i> did!<br><br>I'd heard the hype about this book and seen lots of my book buddies giving it great reviews and five stars, so I knew I had to give a shot asap. And I'm so pleased I did.<br><br>As much as I adore NA and adult romance, there is something warm and fuzzy about a great YA romance. The encounters at school, the peer politics, the dances, the bonfires, the sports meets... so much opportunity for drama. And then of course, there's the first love, the virginal heroine, the first kisses, first touches, etc. I absolutely love it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I want to touch you.” His words were against my lips now. “I want to feel what’s mine. What’s always been mine.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850777._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Bully</i> has all of that. This is the archetypal 'bad boy/good girl' story, mixed with the 'childhood friend' and the 'enemies to lovers' story. You get all that, wrapped into one delicious, heart racing package.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Tate, you’re mine, and I’m yours. Every day you’re<br>going to realize that more and more. When you believe it without a doubt, then I’ll have earned your trust.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>The characters in this book are of YA age, and still at school, but it is pretty steamy for a YA. Just a warning.<br><br>So, the story introduces us to Tatum (Tate) who has lived next door to Jared for eight years. As children, they were inseperable, best friends. But then one summer, everything changed and Jared started hating on Tate. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You were the person that turned things right again. With you, I became courageous and free. It was like the part of me that died with my mom came back when I met you, and I didn’t hurt if I knew I had you. Then one day, out of the blue, I lost you, too. The hurt returned, and I felt sick when I saw you hating me. My rainstorm was gone, and you became cruel. There was no explanation. You were just gone. And my heart was ripped open. I missed you."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>She became the victim of his relentless bullying campaign and he made it his mission to make her life hell. <br>Tate leaves her home to live in France for a year and when she comes back, the story really begins.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Isn’t it about time you fought back?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I luuurved Tate when she began to stand up to Jared. Her ball busting, no shit attitude and her quick wit really made me want to punch the air on multiple occasions! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850778.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>K.C., however, I wanted to throttle! K.C. is Tate's best friend and she irritated the shit out of me! She was weak and fickle and just generally a bit of a twat. Who needs enemies. Tate was incredibly forgiving where I would certainly have pulled her hair out by the roots!<br><br>Jared. Hmmm... where to start. He's a complex character. He's soooo mean throughout the first half of the book. I wanted to hate him and I certainly did feel the compulsion to slap him. A lot. But I just couldn't not love him. He's hot, nasty and clearly completely broken.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm sorry," he whispered. "I know I can make this up to you. Don't hate me."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>And don't worry ladies, he does completely redeem himself. You will be totally in love with Jared 'Bully' Trent by the end of this book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850779.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the idea, through this book, that being bullied creates bullies. Ok, maybe that's the wrong word, I don't love that, but it was incredibly thought provoking. Throughout the book, sweet, friendly, kind hearted Tate was becoming more and more bitter and spiteful as she lashed out against those who were wronging her. She was becoming the bully. Intentionally causing pain to others. It's a strong message that all bullies are just human beings and something along their journey has made them the way they are. The idea that this knock on effect from the catalyst of one person's pain, can cause a downward spiral of heartache and hatred in others. Where does that end? It's no excuse and certainly, bullying cannot be condoned in any capacity, but it's an eye opening thought.<br><br>The sexual tension in this book just absolutely rolled off of the pages. One minute he's spreading rumours about her, then he's kissing her, then he's telling her he doesn't care if she's dead or alive, then he's all over her like a rash. Whiplash, much?! This is a perfect example of the silly boy, who fancies the girl, pulling her pigtails in the playground. Magnified by one hundred!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850780.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Three times I honestly thought I might spontaneously combust... all I'll say is, kitchen, race night and science lab. Pheeewwww! And that's before they even get their shit together.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"If I ever lay my hands on you," he said low and husky, "You'll want it."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>So, clearly, I really loved this book. Duh. Lol. I implore you all to go out and add to your TBR lists, if you haven't already, buy it, download it, whatever... and read it! It's absolutely great and I'm soooo looking forward to book #2, which I believe is Jared's best friend, Madoc's story!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426016i/850781._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><i>Bully</i> Statistics</b><br><b>Steam Rating (out of 5):</b> ♥♥♥♥<br><b>Ending:</b> HEA<br><b>Series:</b> ✓ (<i>Fall Away</i> series)<br><b>Reading Order:</b><br>Book #1 - <i>Bully</i><br>Book #2 - <i>Rival</i> (Not yet released)<br><b>Can this be read as a standalone?</b> Yes<br><b>Themes:</b><br>Bullying<br>Hate-to-love<br>Childhood sweetheart<br>Second chance<br>Abuse<br>First love<br><b>Warning. This book includes... </b><br>Sexual content<br>Bullying<br>Abuse - verbal &amp; physical<br><b>Writing:</b> Great<br><br>UK AMAZON: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Bully-Fall-Away-1-ebook/dp/B00DGT3VL2/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1374493778&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=bully">http://www.amazon.co.uk/Bully-Fall-Aw...</a><br>US AMAZON: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/Bully-Fall-Away-1-ebook/dp/B00DGT3VL2/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1374493778&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=bully">http://www.amazon.com/Bully-Fall-Away...</a><br><br><b>
  <i>Like This Review...?</i>
</b><br>To read more reviews go to my Book Blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://smittensbookblog.wordpress.com/">http://smittensbookblog.wordpress.com/</a><br>Follow me on Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SmittenSC">https://twitter.com/SmittenSC</a><br>Find me on Pinterest: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pinterest.com/smittensc/">http://pinterest.com/smittensc/</a><br>'Like' me on Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/SmittensBookBlog">https://www.facebook.com/SmittensBook...</a></span>

<div id="review_1786295701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1786295701" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1786295701?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1786295701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7942457206082494304">Find me on <a href='http://www.instagram.com/readwithmikee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> & <a href='http://www.twitter.com/readwithmikee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a>!<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝Yesterday lasts forever.<br/>Tomorrow comes never.<br/>Until you.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>As some of you may remember, my experience with my first Penelope Douglas book was disastrous. I absolutely despised Corrupt and I almost promised to never to pick up a book by Penelope Douglas ever again if Corrupt was any indication of what her other books were about. But everyone kept telling me to go for Bully because it seemed to be everyone's favorite.<br/><br/>After putting it off for about a year, I</span>
  <span id="freeText7942457206082494304" style="display:none">Find me on <a href="http://www.instagram.com/readwithmikee" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> &amp; <a href="http://www.twitter.com/readwithmikee" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>!<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝Yesterday lasts forever.<br />Tomorrow comes never.<br />Until you.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />As some of you may remember, my experience with my first Penelope Douglas book was disastrous. I absolutely despised Corrupt and I almost promised to never to pick up a book by Penelope Douglas ever again if Corrupt was any indication of what her other books were about. But everyone kept telling me to go for Bully because it seemed to be everyone's favorite.<br /><br />After putting it off for about a year, I finally plucked up the courage to give this book a try and I absolutely loved it. There was never a dull moment while reading this book. I was hesitant as could be going into Bully because, of course, my experience with Corrupt, but also because I wasn't sure how bullying would be handled in the story. I already had the mindset that if the male character was bullying the main character to the extreme and we're later on forced to believe in their romance, then I was going to DNF this book right away. Thankfully, it wasn't like that. Bullying was, involved but it wasn't too bad. Not that bullying is ever good or anything, but I've seen real people do and say worse. I was expecting the absolute worst form of bullying but it wasn't taken too far and I actually appreciate that.<br /><br />Basically, the thing that made this book for me was Tate, our main character. Praise, Jesus! We finally got a female character that wasn't afraid to fight back! I thought I was going end up hating Tate if she turned out to be another pushover but thank goodness she was far from that. She was kicking ass and throwing punches. Hell yeah! I wish we had more females in romance books that actually stood up for themselves and/or don't let people walk all over them. Authors take note!<br /><br />As for Jared, I suppose he was one of the better male characters I've read about in awhile. Yes, he was an asshole but I warmed up to him, which doesn't happen often anymore when it comes to romance books.<br /><br />Overall, Bully really exceeded my expectations. I did not expect to enjoy it this much or even at all since I've been having a bad streak with romance novels lately but it was like a breath of fresh air finally reading a romance book that I enjoyed. I think it helped that I didn't set my expectations so high after the disappointment that was Corrupt. But this book really redeemed Penelope Douglas to me as a romance author and because of Bully, I'll definitely be giving the rest of this series a shot along with Penelope's future books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7942457206082494304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2043205745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043205745" />
    <a title="chan ☆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48727754-chan"><img alt="chan ☆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596680961p2/48727754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043205745?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chan ☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chan ☆" href="/user/show/48727754-chan">chan ☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043205745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2373053095488698305">reread 11/24/19: all my thoughts are pretty much the same as the first time but especially the bit about p. douglas books working SO MUCH BETTER as dual POV. kept wanting jared's thoughts but he remains kinda one note because we don't get his POV. not bad, not my fave of hers'.<br/><br/>--------------------<br/><br/><i>I was hoping we could move forward without looking back.</i><br/><br/><b>the good</b><br/>This is my second book by Penelope Douglas and wow was it a trip. This book focuses on the former friendship and hate-to-love relationship</span>
  <span id="freeText2373053095488698305" style="display:none">reread 11/24/19: all my thoughts are pretty much the same as the first time but especially the bit about p. douglas books working SO MUCH BETTER as dual POV. kept wanting jared's thoughts but he remains kinda one note because we don't get his POV. not bad, not my fave of hers'.<br /><br />--------------------<br /><br /><i>I was hoping we could move forward without looking back.</i><br /><br /><b>the good</b><br />This is my second book by Penelope Douglas and wow was it a trip. This book focuses on the former friendship and hate-to-love relationship between Tate and Jared. Tate and Jared were friends in middle school until he went away the summer before high school. He comes back changed, and bullies Tate by spreading rumors and teasing her.<br /><br />What I loved about this book was the level of introspection that Douglas manages to add to her stories. For me, I can't relate to a character unless I can get inside their head. I also find it hard to justify shitty behavior if they don't explain it as well. Tate's reactions to her treatment are complex and make sense given the circumstances. She's a well fleshed out character and I definitely wanted her to get what she wanted.<br /><br /><b>the bad</b><br />While this was my second book by this author I believe it was the first one she ever wrote. And it definitely shows. If anything I am incredibly impressed in how her caliber of writing has changed over a 3 year span but this book had a lot of bad NA tropes. Namely, the attitude of Tate towards other females in the book. She becomes incredibly possessive of a guy she's not with and tears down her friend because of it. AND!!!!! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She beats up another female out of jealousy! Yeah the girl was written as a bitch but holy shit. Violence was not the answer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I also think that Punk 57 worked so well (and a lot of other NAs do too) because it had dual narration. In this one, it was REALLY hard to sympathize with the love interest because he was a dick but you couldn't really figure out why until the end of the book. I am ALL for the hate-to-love trope if it's done well but it wasn't that convincing in this book. Bullying your former friend for almost all of high school is more than just a little psychotic and the explanation given, while heartbreaking just doesn't really add up. The quote I included in this review was a direct result of this... how do you expect someone to look forward after the torment you've caused them without stopping to ask more questions???<br /><br />I definitely didn't hate this book, and I sped through it because it kept me entertained. But I'm going to have to read more from this series before I really pass judgment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2373053095488698305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1306105985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1306105985" />
    <a title="Andie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30510075-andie"><img alt="Andie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477111902p2/30510075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306105985?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andie " href="/user/show/30510075-andie">Andie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30510075-andie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30510075-andie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30510075-andie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30510075-andie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306105985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9696578189128200748"><b>LOVE LOVE LOVE!!! 5 STOMACH KNOTTING STARS!</b><br/><br/>Although it was hard to watch the torment this girl goes through at the hand of one boy, I absolutely loooved this book!! It was so well written, it was hard for me to believe this was a debut novel. I started Bully around midnight two nights ago to help tire my eyes out. Well one thing led to another and next thing I knew, it was 5:00 am. Sleep was completely forgotten as I made my way through the entire book in one sitting! I couldn't stop reading eve</span>
  <span id="freeText9696578189128200748" style="display:none"><b>LOVE LOVE LOVE!!! 5 STOMACH KNOTTING STARS!</b><br /><br />Although it was hard to watch the torment this girl goes through at the hand of one boy, I absolutely loooved this book!! It was so well written, it was hard for me to believe this was a debut novel. I started Bully around midnight two nights ago to help tire my eyes out. Well one thing led to another and next thing I knew, it was 5:00 am. Sleep was completely forgotten as I made my way through the entire book in one sitting! I couldn't stop reading even when I wanted to! I'm a sucker for angst, drama, and a ton of sexual tension. Bully not only met those requirements but exceeded them!<br /><br />Tate and Jared used to be inseparable. They were there for each other through hard times, they were best friends. Until the summer before their Freshman year. Jared goes to stay with his dad for the summer and comes home different. He was once a kind and caring boy. Now he's cold, volatile, and cruel. Jared becomes Tate's own personal bully. For two years, Jared has never missed the chance to embarrass and humiliate her and Tate has no clue why. Tate decides to go to France for her Junior year for a study abroad program to get away from it all. But she's back now for her senior year and has decided enough is enough. It's time to fight back.<br /><br />Jared is the schools walking one night stand. He's gorgeous, popular, and maybe even feared a little bit. But Jared is sitting on his secret from that summer. A secret that has haunted him and made him crave revenge. Since he can't hurt the one he truly wants to hurt, he takes his rage out the only way he knows how. Reflecting his hurt and anger on the one person he ever loved. <br /><br />The things Jared says and does to Tate are despicable. He goes to great lengths to make Tate's life hell. From rumors, pranks, and sabotage to downright hurtful words. Tate started out as a timid girl and hid from Jared at all costs. But after her year in France, she came back swinging. I loved seeing her stand up for herself and dishing it out to those who ridiculed her. There were times where Tate flirted with the edge of sticking up for herself and becoming a bully herself. <br /><br /><b>"This is what bullies are made of"</b> became a mantra in her head.<br /><br />As Tate and Jared come head to head with each other, things start to change. Sexual tension between the two is very obvious. Secrets are revealed and they become even closer. But can Tate ever forgive Jared after everything? Can she ever trust him again? SHOULD she trust him again?! There's a very fine line between love and hate. <br /><br />I shouldn't love Jared right?? Oh but I do. I spent most of the book loving to hate him, but still kind of loving him at the same time. Call me crazy, but by the end I just really loved him. Do I think Tate should trust him though? Probably not. Even after secrets come out, I don't justify Jared's actions...There is never an excuse to bullying, just to be clear! But then again, I can't say what I'd do in this situation because like I already said, there's a fine line between love and hate.<br /><br />I spent the entirety of this book with my stomach pounding in my chest and a constant lump in my throat! Pages seemed to turn themselves. There was no way I could put this book down until I knew how it ended. The story was gripping, addictive, exciting, and a roller coaster of emotions. The chemistry between the characters was very real and intense. At times I felt like I was Tate. I could feel her love, hate, embarrassment, and inner turmoil. I'm so excited to know that there is another book from Jared's eyes. I can't wait to know him better. I recommend this book to anyone who's a fan of angst and drama because this is without a doubt one of the best I've read. I think people who love the After series by Anna Todd and Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry will love Bully. I don't recommend this to anyone under the age of 17 for some explicit scenes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9696578189128200748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZrXPYDIFCQbj0gB90z2dknzHuMMpRW2L9qnTCy0wEdox1LC2NOfSsHJNwfF1bf7zjBZAcz7rhGEbtLiXEczsxQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bR1O9+05Nh3cc+b2oE4j+WXuWDSLqszbemdJT8uhhX86fDEh69vtq03sJ3oGHkCYlT+ghJwEJTGXeiLT9114YA==')})
  }

Fate has brought K.C. back into his life—except what he thought was a great twist of luck turns out to be too close for comfort. As the bond between them grows, he discovers that convincing K.C. to get out from her mother’s shadow is hard, but revealing the darkest parts of his soul is nearly impossible.…<\/span>\n  <a       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/25420107-bully">Quotes from Bully</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I like storms. Thunder torrential rain, puddles, wet shoes. When the clouds roll in, I get filled with this giddy expectation. Everything is more beautiful in the rain. Don't ask me why. But it’s like this whole other realm of opportunity. I used to feel like a superhero, riding my bike over the dangerously slick roads, or maybe an Olympic athlete enduring rough trials to make it to the finish line. On sunny days, as a girl, I could still wake up to that thrilled feeling. You made me giddy with expectation, just like a symphonic rainstorm. You were a tempest in the sun, the thunder in a boring, cloudless sky. I remember I’d shovel in my breakfast as fast as I could, so I could go knock on your door. We’d play all day, only coming back for food and sleep. We played hide and seek, you’d push me on the swing, or we’d climb trees. Being your sidekick gave me a sense of home again. You see, when I was ten, my mom died. She had cancer, and I lost her before I really knew her. My world felt so insecure, and I was scared. You were the person that turned things right again. With you, I became courageous and free. It was like the part of me that died with my mom came back when I met you, and I didn’t hurt if I knew I had you. Then one day, out of the blue, I lost you, too. The hurt returned, and I felt sick when I saw you hating me. My rainstorm was gone, and you became cruel. There was no explanation. You were just gone. And my heart was ripped open. I missed you. I missed my mom. What was worse than losing you, was when you started to hurt me. Your words and actions made me hate coming to school. They made me uncomfortable in my own home. Everything still hurts, but I know none of it is my fault. There are a lot of words that I could use to describe you, but the only one that includes sad, angry, miserable, and pitiful is “coward.” I a year, I’ll be gone, and you’ll be nothing but some washout whose height of existence was in high school. You were my tempest, my thunder cloud, my tree in the downpour. I loved all those things, and I loved you. But now? You’re a fucking drought. I thought that all the assholes drove German cars, but it turns out that pricks in Mustangs can still leave scars.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/835942-i-like-storms-thunder-torrential-rain-puddles-wet-shoes-when">733 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
